      </a>\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Right-_and_left-hand_traffic" title="Right- and left-hand traffic">\n          right\n         </a>\n      </th>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%2B261" title="+261">\n          +261\n         </a>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bradtp2_9-1">\n          <a          ISO 3166 code\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-2:MG" title="ISO 3166-2:MG">\n          MG\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         <a href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">\n          Internet TLD\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/.mg" title=".mg">\n          .mg\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Madagascar\n       </b>\n       (\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">\n         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">\n          /\n          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">\n           <span title="/\xcb\x8c/: secondary stress follows">\n            \xcb\x8c\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'m\' in \'my\'">\n            m\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc3\xa6/: \'a\' in \'bad\'">\n            \xc3\xa6\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'d\' in \'dye\'">\n            d\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\x99/: \'a\' in \'about\'">\n            \xc9\x99\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\n            \xcb\x88\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\xa1/: \'g\' in \'guy\'">\n            \xc9\xa1\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc3\xa6/: \'a\' in \'bad\'">\n            \xc3\xa6\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'s\' in \'sigh\'">\n            s\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'k\' in \'kind\'">\n            k\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\x99r/: \'er\' in \'letter\'">\n            \xc9\x99r\n           </span>\n          </span>\n          /\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       ;\n       <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_language" title="Malagasy language">\n        Malagasy\n       </a>\n       :\n       <span lang="mg">\n        <i>\n         Madagasikara\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       ), officially the\n       <b>\n        Republic of Madagascar\n       </b>\n       (Malagasy:\n       <span lang="mg">\n        <i>\n         Repoblikan\'i Madagasikara\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Malagasy" title="Help:IPA/Malagasy">\n         [republi\xcb\x88k\xca\xb2an mada\xc9\xa1as\xcb\x88k\xca\xb2ar\xc9\x99\xcc\xa5]\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       ; French:\n       <span lang="fr">\n        <i>\n         R\xc3\xa9publique de Madagascar\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       ), and previously known as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_Republic" title="Malagasy Republic">\n        Malagasy Republic\n       </a>\n       , is an\n       <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">\n        island country\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">\n        Indian Ocean\n       </a>\n       , off the coast of\n       <a href="/wiki/East_Africa" title="East Africa">\n        East Africa\n       </a>\n       . The nation comprises the island of\n       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Madagascar" title="Geography of Madagascar">\n        Madagascar\n       </a>\n       (the fourth-\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_by_area" title="List of islands by area">\n        largest island\n       </a>\n       in the world), and numerous smaller peripheral islands. Following the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prehistoric" title="Prehistoric">\n        prehistoric\n       </a>\n       breakup of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Supercontinent" title="Supercontinent">\n        supercontinent\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Gondwana" title="Gondwana">\n        Gondwana\n       </a>\n       , Madagascar split from the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_peninsula" title="Indian peninsula">\n        Indian peninsula\n       </a>\n       around 88\xc2\xa0million years ago, allowing native plants and animals to evolve in relative isolation. Consequently, Madagascar is a\n       <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_hotspot" title="Biodiversity hotspot">\n        biodiversity hotspot\n       </a>\n       ; over 90% of\n       <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Madagascar" title="Wildlife of Madagascar">\n        its wildlife\n       </a>\n       is found nowhere else on Earth. The island\'s diverse ecosystems and unique wildlife are threatened by the encroachment of the rapidly growing human population and other environmental threats.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The first\n       <a href="/wiki/Archaeology" title="Archaeology">\n        archaeological\n       </a>\n       evidence for human foraging on Madagascar dates to 2000\xc2\xa0BC. Human settlement of Madagascar occurred between 350\xc2\xa0BC and AD\xc2\xa0550 by\n       <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_peoples" title="Austronesian peoples">\n        Austronesian peoples\n       </a>\n       arriving on\n       <a href="/wiki/Outrigger_canoe" title="Outrigger canoe">\n        outrigger canoes\n       </a>\n       from\n       <a href="/wiki/Borneo" title="Borneo">\n        Borneo\n       </a>\n       . These were joined around AD 1000 by\n       <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">\n        Bantu\n       </a>\n       migrants crossing the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mozambique_Channel" title="Mozambique Channel">\n        Mozambique Channel\n       </a>\n       from East Africa. Other groups continued to settle on Madagascar over time, each one making lasting contributions to Malagasy cultural life. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_people" title="Malagasy people">\n        Malagasy ethnic group\n       </a>\n       is often divided into 18 or more\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_of_Madagascar" title="Ethnic groups of Madagascar">\n        sub-groups\n       </a>\n       of which the largest are the\n       <a href="/wiki/Merina_people" title="Merina people">\n        Merina\n       </a>\n       of the central highlands.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Until the late 18th century, the island of Madagascar was ruled by a fragmented assortment of shifting sociopolitical alliances. Beginning in the early 19th century, most of the island was united and ruled as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Merina_Kingdom" title="Merina Kingdom">\n        Kingdom of Madagascar\n       </a>\n       by a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Malagasy_monarchs" title="List of Malagasy monarchs">\n        series\n       </a>\n       of Merina\n       <a href="/wiki/Andriana" title="Andriana">\n        nobles\n       </a>\n       . The monarchy collapsed in 1897 when the island was absorbed into the\n       <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">\n        French colonial empire\n       </a>\n       , from which the island gained independence in 1960. The autonomous state of Madagascar has since undergone four major constitutional periods, termed republics. Since 1992, the nation has officially been governed as a constitutional democracy from its capital at\n       <a href="/wiki/Antananarivo" title="Antananarivo">\n        Antananarivo\n       </a>\n       . However, in a\n       <a href="/wiki/2009_Malagasy_political_crisis" title="2009 Malagasy political crisis">\n        popular uprising in 2009\n       </a>\n       , president\n       <a href="/wiki/Marc_Ravalomanana" title="Marc Ravalomanana">\n        Marc Ravalomanana\n       </a>\n       was made to resign and presidential power was transferred in March 2009 to\n       <a href="/wiki/Andry_Rajoelina" title="Andry Rajoelina">\n        Andry Rajoelina\n       </a>\n       . Constitutional governance was restored in January 2014, when\n       <a href="/wiki/Hery_Rajaonarimampianina" title="Hery Rajaonarimampianina">\n        Hery Rajaonarimampianina\n       </a>\n       was named president following a\n       <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_general_election,_2013" title="Malagasy general election, 2013">\n        2013 election\n       </a>\n       deemed fair and transparent by the international community. Madagascar is a member of the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">\n        United Nations\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">\n        African Union\n       </a>\n       (AU), the\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">\n        Southern African Development Community\n       </a>\n       (SADC), and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organisation_Internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation Internationale de la Francophonie">\n        Organisation Internationale de la Francophonie\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Madagascar belongs to the group of least developed countries, according to the United Nations.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_language" title="Malagasy language">\n        Malagasy\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">\n        French\n       </a>\n       are both\n       <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">\n        official languages\n       </a>\n       of the state. The majority of the population adheres to\n       <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_mythology" title="Malagasy mythology">\n        traditional beliefs\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Madagascar" title="Christianity in Madagascar">\n        Christianity\n       </a>\n       , or an amalgamation of both. Ecotourism and agriculture, paired with greater investments in education, health, and private enterprise, are key elements of Madagascar\'s development strategy. Under Ravalomanana, these investments produced substantial economic growth, but the benefits were not evenly spread throughout the population, producing tensions over the increasing cost of living and declining living standards among the poor and some segments of the middle class. As of 2017\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , the economy has been weakened by the 2009\xe2\x80\x932013 political crisis, and quality of life remains low for the majority of the Malagasy population.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2">\n         <a href="#Geography">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           2\n          </span>\n Ecology\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5">\n           <a href="#Environmental_issues">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n       </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Kingdom of Madagascar\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10">\n  </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Independent state\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1    </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13">\n           <a href="#Structure">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             4.1\n            </span>\n class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15">\n           <a href="#Security">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             4.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Security\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16">\n           <a href="#Administrative_divisions">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             4.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Administrative divisions\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17">\n           <a href="#United_Nations_involvement">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             4.5\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             United Nations involvement\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18">\n   <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19">\n           <a href="#Natural_resources_and_trade">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Natural resources and trade\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20">\n           <a </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21">\n         <a href="#Health">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           6\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Health\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22">\n         <a href="#Education">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           7\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Education\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23">\n         <a href="#Demographics">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Demographics\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24">\n           <a href="#Ethnic_groups">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             8.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Ethnic groups\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25">\n           <a href="#Languages">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             8.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Languages\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26">\n           <a href="#Religion">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             8.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Religion\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27">\n         <a href="#Culture">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           9\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Culture\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28">\n         <a href="#Arts">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           10\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Arts\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29">\n           <a href="#Sport_and_recreation">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             10.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Sport and recreation\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30">\n           <a href="#Cuisine">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             10.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Cuisine\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           11\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32">\n         <a href="#Notes">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           12\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Notes\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           13\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           14\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">\n        Etymology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       In the\n       <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_language" title="Malagasy language">\n        Malagasy language\n       </a>\n       , the island of Madagascar is called\n       <i>\n        Madagasikara\n       </i>\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Malagasy" title="Help:IPA/Malagasy">\n         [mada\xc9\xa1as\xca\xb2\xcb\x88k\xca\xb2ar\xc9\x99\xcc\xa5]\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       and its people are referred to as\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_people" title="Malagasy people">\n         Malagasy\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NatGeo1_11-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NatGeo1-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The island\'s appellation "Madagascar" is not of local origin, but rather was popularized in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">\n        Middle Ages\n       </a>\n       by Europeans.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cousins_12-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Cousins-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The name\n       <i>\n        Madageiscar\n       </i>\n       was first recorded in the memoirs of 13th-century Venetian explorer\n       <a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo" title="Marco Polo">\n        Marco Polo\n       </a>\n       as a corrupted\n       <a href="/wiki/Transliteration" title="Transliteration">\n        transliteration\n       </a>\n       of the name\n       <a href="/wiki/Mogadishu" title="Mogadishu">\n        Mogadishu\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">\n        Somali\n       </a>\n       port with which Polo had confused the island.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Room_2006.2C_p._230_13-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Room_2006.2C_p._230-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lawrence_of_Rome" title="Lawrence of Rome">\n        St. Laurence\n       </a>\n       \'s Day in 1500, Portuguese explorer\n       <a href="/wiki/Diogo_Dias" title="Diogo Dias">\n        Diogo Dias\n       </a>\n       landed on the island and named it\n       <i>\n        S\xc3\xa3o Louren\xc3\xa7o\n       </i>\n       . Polo\'s name was preferred and popularized on\n       <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">\n        Renaissance\n       </a>\n       maps. No single Malagasy-language name predating\n       <i>\n        Madagasikara\n       </i>\n       appears to have been used by the local population to refer to the island, although some communities had their own name for part or all of the land they inhabited.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Room_2006.2C_p._230_13-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Room_2006.2C_p._230-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">\n        Geography\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Madagascar" title="Geography of Madagascar">\n        Geography of Madagascar\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:537px;max-width:537px">\n        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Imerina_countryside_riziere_rice_paddies_Madagascar.jpg">\n           <img alt="terraced emerald paddy fields checker softly rolling hills" data-file-height="656" data-file-width="1023" height="115" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Imerina_countryside_riziere_rice_paddies_Madagascar.jpg/180px-Imerina_countryside_riziere_rice_paddies_Madagascar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Imerina_countryside_riziere_rice_paddies_Madagascar.jpg/270px-Imerina_countryside_riziere_rice_paddies_Madagascar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Imerina_countryside_riziere_rice_paddies_Madagascar.jpg/360px-Imerina_countryside_riziere_rice_paddies_Madagascar.jpg 2x" width="180"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:192px;max-width:192px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rainforestmadagascar04.tif">\n           <img alt="Hills covered with dense blue green tropical forests" data-file-height="945" data-file-width="1535" height="117" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Rainforestmadagascar04.tif/lossless-page1-190px-Rainforestmadagascar04.tif.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Rainforestmadagascar04.tif/lossless-page1-285px-Rainforestmadagascar04.tif.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Rainforestmadagascar04.tif/lossless-page1-380px-Rainforestmadagascar04.tif.png 2x" width="190"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:157px;max-width:157px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Beach_in_Madagascar_with_pirogues_and_palm_trees.jpg">\n           <img alt="White sand beach lined with palm trees along a turquoise sea" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Beach_in_Madagascar_with_pirogues_and_palm_trees.jpg/155px-Beach_in_Madagascar_with_pirogues_and_palm_trees.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Beach_in_Madagascar_with_pirogues_and_palm_trees.jpg/233px-Beach_in_Madagascar_with_pirogues_and_palm_trees.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Beach_in_Madagascar_with_pirogues_and_palm_trees.jpg/310px-Beach_in_Madagascar_with_pirogues_and_palm_trees.jpg 2x" width="155"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div style="clear:left">\n        </div>\n        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">\n         The terraced paddy fields of the\n         <a href="/wiki/Central_Highlands_(Madagascar)" title="Central Highlands (Madagascar)">\n          central highlands\n         </a>\n         of Madagascar (left) give way to tropical rainforest along the eastern coast (center) bordered by the shores of the\n         <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">\n          Indian Ocean\n         </a>\n         (right).\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       At 592,800 square kilometres (228,900\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BGNote_14-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BGNote-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Madagascar is the world\'s 47th\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Largest_country" title="Largest country">\n        largest country\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_15-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-cia-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_by_area" title="List of islands by area">\n        fourth-largest island\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BGNote_14-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BGNote-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The country lies mostly between latitudes\n       <a href="/wiki/12th_parallel_south" title="12th parallel south">\n        12\xc2\xb0S\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/26th_parallel_south" title="26th parallel south">\n        26\xc2\xb0S\n       </a>\n       , and longitudes\n       <a href="/wiki/43rd_meridian_east" title="43rd meridian east">\n        43\xc2\xb0E\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/51st_meridian_east" title="51st meridian east">\n        51\xc2\xb0E\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-georeport_16-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-georeport-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Neighboring islands include the French territory of\n       <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="R\xc3\xa9union">\n        R\xc3\xa9union\n       </a>\n       and the country of\n       <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">\n        Mauritius\n       </a>\n       to the east, as well as the state of\n       <a href="/wiki/Comoros" title="Comoros">\n        Comoros\n       </a>\n       and the French territory of\n       <a href="/wiki/Mayotte" title="Mayotte">\n        Mayotte\n       </a>\n       to the north west. The nearest mainland state is\n       <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">\n        Mozambique\n       </a>\n       , located to the west.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The prehistoric breakup of the supercontinent\n       <a href="/wiki/Gondwana" title="Gondwana">\n        Gondwana\n       </a>\n       separated the Madagascar\xe2\x80\x93Antarctica\xe2\x80\x93India landmass from the Africa\xe2\x80\x93South America landmass around 135\xc2\xa0million years ago. Madagascar later split from India about 88\xc2\xa0million years ago, allowing plants and animals on the island to evolve in relative isolation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Along the length of the eastern coast runs a narrow and steep\n       <a href="/wiki/Escarpment" title="Escarpment">\n        escarpment\n       </a>\n       containing much of the island\'s remaining tropical\n       <a href="/wiki/Madagascar_lowland_forests" title="Madagascar lowland forests">\n        lowland forest\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       To the west of this ridge lies a\n       <a href="/wiki/Plateau" title="Plateau">\n        plateau\n       </a>\n       in the center of the island ranging in altitude from 750 to 1,500\xc2\xa0m (2,460 to 4,920\xc2\xa0ft) above sea level. These\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_Highlands_(Madagascar)" title="Central Highlands (Madagascar)">\n        central highlands\n       </a>\n       , traditionally the homeland of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Merina_people" title="Merina people">\n        Merina people\n       </a>\n       and the location of their historic capital at\n       <a href="/wiki/Antananarivo" title="Antananarivo">\n        Antananarivo\n       </a>\n       , are the most densely populated part of the island and are characterized by terraced, rice-growing valleys lying between grassy hills and patches of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Madagascar_subhumid_forests" title="Madagascar subhumid forests">\n        subhumid forests\n       </a>\n       that formerly covered the highland region. To the west of the highlands, the increasingly arid terrain gradually slopes down to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mozambique_Channel" title="Mozambique Channel">\n        Mozambique Channel\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Madagascar_mangroves" title="Madagascar mangroves">\n        mangrove swamps\n       </a>\n       along the coast.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-endemicstats_18-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-endemicstats-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:505px;max-width:505px">\n        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:165px;max-width:165px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Isalo_canyons.jpg">\n           <img alt="Pastel striated stone outcroppings jut from the plains" data-file-height="1452" data-file-width="2092" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Isalo_canyons.jpg/163px-Isalo_canyons.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Isalo_canyons.jpg/245px-Isalo_canyons.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Isalo_canyons.jpg/326px-Isalo_canyons.jpg 2x" width="163"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:157px;max-width:157px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:All%C3%A9e_des_Baobabs_near_Morondava,_Madagascar.jpg">\n           <img alt="Giant baobabs clustered against the sky" data-file-height="1276" data-file-width="1701" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/All%C3%A9e_des_Baobabs_near_Morondava%2C_Madagascar.jpg/155px-All%C3%A9e_des_Baobabs_near_Morondava%2C_Madagascar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/All%C3%A9e_des_Baobabs_near_Morondava%2C_Madagascar.jpg/233px-All%C3%A9e_des_Baobabs_near_Morondava%2C_Madagascar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/All%C3%A9e_des_Baobabs_near_Morondava%2C_Madagascar.jpg/310px-All%C3%A9e_des_Baobabs_near_Morondava%2C_Madagascar.jpg 2x" width="155"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:177px;max-width:177px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spiny_Forest_Ifaty_Madagascar.jpg">\n           <img alt="Bizarre succulents growing sparsely from deep red earth" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" height="117" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Spiny_Forest_Ifaty_Madagascar.jpg/175px-Spiny_Forest_Ifaty_Madagascar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Spiny_Forest_Ifaty_Madagascar.jpg/263px-Spiny_Forest_Ifaty_Madagascar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Spiny_Forest_Ifaty_Madagascar.jpg/350px-Spiny_Forest_Ifaty_Madagascar.jpg 2x" width="175"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div style="clear:left">\n        </div>\n        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">\n         The grassy plains that dominate the western landscape are dotted with stony massifs (left), patches of deciduous forest, and\n         <a href="/wiki/Avenue_of_the_Baobabs" title="Avenue of the Baobabs">\n          baobab trees\n         </a>\n         (center), while the south is characterized by desert and\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madagascar_spiny_thickets" title="Madagascar spiny thickets">\n          spiny forests\n         </a>\n         (right).\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Madagascar\'s highest peaks rise from three prominent highland\n       <a href="/wiki/Massif" title="Massif">\n        massifs\n       </a>\n       :\n       <a href="/wiki/Maromokotro" title="Maromokotro">\n        Maromokotro\n       </a>\n       2,876\xc2\xa0m (9,436\xc2\xa0ft) in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tsaratanana_Massif#Tsaranoro_Massif" title="Tsaratanana Massif">\n        Tsaratanana Massif\n       </a>\n       is the island\'s highest point, followed by Boby Peak 2,658\xc2\xa0m (8,720\xc2\xa0ft) in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Andringitra_Massif" title="Andringitra Massif">\n        Andringitra Massif\n       </a>\n       , and Tsiafajavona 2,643\xc2\xa0m (8,671\xc2\xa0ft) in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ankaratra" title="Ankaratra">\n        Ankaratra\n       </a>\n       Massif. To the east, the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Canal_des_Pangalanes" title="Canal des Pangalanes">\n         Canal des Pangalanes\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       is a chain of man-made and natural lakes connected by canals built by the French just inland from the east coast and running parallel to it for some 600\xc2\xa0km (370\xc2\xa0mi).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EBLand_19-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EBLand-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The western and southern sides, which lie in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Rain_shadow" title="Rain shadow">\n        rain shadow\n       </a>\n       of the central highlands, are home to\n       <a href="/wiki/Madagascar_dry_deciduous_forests" title="Madagascar dry deciduous forests">\n        dry deciduous forests\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madagascar_spiny_thickets" title="Madagascar spiny thickets">\n        spiny forests\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Deserts_and_xeric_shrublands" title="Deserts and xeric shrublands">\n        deserts and xeric shrublands\n       </a>\n       . Due to their lower population densities, Madagascar\'s dry deciduous forests have been better preserved than the eastern rain forests or the original woodlands of the central plateau. The western coast features many protected harbors, but silting is a major problem caused by\n       <a href="/wiki/Sediment" title="Sediment">\n        sediment\n       </a>\n       from the high levels of inland\n       <a href="/wiki/Erosion" title="Erosion">\n        erosion\n       </a>\n       carried by rivers crossing the broad western plains.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EBLand_19-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EBLand-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">\n        Climate\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Climate">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Madagascar_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1900" data-file-width="1900" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Madagascar_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/220px-Madagascar_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Madagascar_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/330px-Madagascar_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Madagascar_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/440px-Madagascar_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Madagascar_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A\n         <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">\n          K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification\n         </a>\n         map of Madagascar\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Biogeographic_timetable_of_Madagascar_-_journal.pone.0062086.g003.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4163" data-file-width="2925" height="242" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Biogeographic_timetable_of_Madagascar_-_journal.pone.0062086.g003.png/170px-Biogeographic_timetable_of_Madagascar_-_journal.pone.0062086.g003.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Biogeographic_timetable_of_Madagascar_-_journal.pone.0062086.g003.png/255px-Biogeographic_timetable_of_Madagascar_-_journal.pone.0062086.g003.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Biogeographic_timetable_of_Madagascar_-_journal.pone.0062086.g003.png/340px-Biogeographic_timetable_of_Madagascar_-_journal.pone.0062086.g003.png 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Biogeographic_timetable_of_Madagascar_-_journal.pone.0062086.g003.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Biogeographic timetable of Madagascar over the last 200 million years\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Madagascar#Climate" title="Geography of Madagascar">\n        Geography of Madagascar \xc2\xa7\xc2\xa0Climate\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The combination of southeastern\n       <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">\n        trade winds\n       </a>\n       and northwestern\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monsoons" title="Monsoons">\n        monsoons\n       </a>\n       produces a hot rainy season (November\xe2\x80\x93April) with frequently destructive\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cyclones" title="Cyclones">\n        cyclones\n       </a>\n       , and a relatively cooler dry season (May\xe2\x80\x93October). Rain clouds originating over the Indian Ocean discharge much of their moisture over the island\'s eastern coast; the heavy precipitation supports the area\'s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rain_forest" title="Rain forest">\n        rain forest\n       </a>\n       ecosystem. The central highlands are both drier and cooler while the west is drier still, and a\n       <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">\n        semi-arid climate\n       </a>\n       prevails in the southwest and southern interior of the island.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-endemicstats_18-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-endemicstats-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">\n        Tropical cyclones\n       </a>\n       annually cause damage to infrastructure and local economies as well as loss of life.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_20-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LOC-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2004\n       <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Gafilo" title="Cyclone Gafilo">\n        Cyclone Gafilo\n       </a>\n       became the strongest cyclone ever recorded to hit Madagascar. The storm killed 172 people, left 214,260 homeless\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gafilo_21-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-gafilo-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and caused more than US$250\xc2\xa0million in damage.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_22-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">\n        Ecology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Ecology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Madagascar" title="Wildlife of Madagascar">\n        Wildlife of Madagascar\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Flora_of_Madagascar" title="Flora of Madagascar">\n        Flora of Madagascar\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Fauna_of_Madagascar" title="Fauna of Madagascar">\n        Fauna of Madagascar\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agroecology_in_Madagascar" title="Agroecology in Madagascar">\n        Agroecology in Madagascar\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ecoregions_of_Madagascar" title="Ecoregions of Madagascar">\n        Ecoregions of Madagascar\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_Madagascar" title="List of World Heritage Sites in Madagascar">\n        List of World Heritage Sites in Madagascar\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ravenala_madagascariensis_Maui.jpg">\n         <img alt="tall, fan-like palm tree" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1535" data-file-width="1152" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Ravenala_madagascariensis_Maui.jpg/170px-Ravenala_madagascariensis_Maui.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Ravenala_madagascariensis_Maui.jpg/255px-Ravenala_madagascariensis_Maui.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Ravenala_madagascariensis_Maui.jpg/340px-Ravenala_madagascariensis_Maui.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ravenala_madagascariensis_Maui.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The island\'s iconic\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ravenala_madagascariensis" title="Ravenala madagascariensis">\n          traveller\'s palm\n         </a>\n         (\n         <i>\n          ravinala\n         </i>\n         ) features in the national emblem.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       As a result of the island\'s long isolation from neighboring continents, Madagascar is home to an abundance of plants and animals found nowhere else on Earth.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIHotSpot_23-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CIHotSpot-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tattersall_24-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tattersall-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Approximately 90% of all plant and animal species found in Madagascar are\n       <a href="/wiki/Endemism" title="Endemism">\n        endemic\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       including the\n       <a href="/wiki/Lemur" title="Lemur">\n        lemurs\n       </a>\n       (a type of\n       <a href="/wiki/Strepsirrhini" title="Strepsirrhini">\n        strepsirrhine\n       </a>\n       primate), the carnivorous\n       <a href="/wiki/Fossa_(animal)" title="Fossa (animal)">\n        fossa\n       </a>\n       and many birds. This distinctive ecology has led some ecologists to refer to Madagascar as the "eighth continent",\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the island has been classified by\n       <a href="/wiki/Conservation_International" title="Conservation International">\n        Conservation International\n       </a>\n       as a biodiversity hotspot.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIHotSpot_23-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CIHotSpot-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       More than 80\xc2\xa0percent of Madagascar\'s 14,883\n       <a href="/wiki/Flora_of_Madagascar" title="Flora of Madagascar">\n        plant species\n       </a>\n       are found nowhere else in the world, including five plant families.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-endemism_27-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-endemism-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The family\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Didiereaceae" title="Didiereaceae">\n         Didiereaceae\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , composed of four genera and 11 species, is limited to the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madagascar_spiny_thickets" title="Madagascar spiny thickets">\n        spiny forests\n       </a>\n       of southwestern Madagascar.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-endemicstats_18-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-endemicstats-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Four-fifths of the world\'s\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Pachypodium" title="Pachypodium">\n         Pachypodium\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       species are endemic to the island.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Three-fourths\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-B2011plant_29-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-B2011plant-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       of Madagascar\'s 860\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-endemism_27-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-endemism-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orchid" title="Orchid">\n        orchid\n       </a>\n       species are found here alone, as are six of the world\'s nine\n       <a href="/wiki/Adansonia" title="Adansonia">\n        baobab\n       </a>\n       species.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">\n        <a href="#cite_note-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The island is home to around 170 palm species, three times as many as on all of mainland Africa; 165 of them are endemic.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-B2011plant_29-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-B2011plant-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Many native plant species are used as herbal remedies for a variety of afflictions. The drugs\n       <a href="/wiki/Vinblastine" title="Vinblastine">\n        vinblastine\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MoleculesReview_31-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MoleculesReview-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Vincristine" title="Vincristine">\n        vincristine\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MoleculesReview_31-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MoleculesReview-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       are\n       <a href="/wiki/Vinca_alkaloid" title="Vinca alkaloid">\n        <i>\n         vinca\n        </i>\n        alkaloids\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       used to treat\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hodgkin%27s_disease" title="Hodgkin\'s disease">\n        Hodgkin\'s disease\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Leukemia" title="Leukemia">\n        leukemia\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and other cancers,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       were derived from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Catharanthus" title="Catharanthus">\n        Madagascar periwinkle\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-periw_39-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-periw-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ravenala_madagascariensis" title="Ravenala madagascariensis">\n        traveler\'s palm\n       </a>\n       , known locally as\n       <i>\n        ravinala\n       </i>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and endemic to the eastern rain forests,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       is highly iconic of Madagascar and is featured in the national emblem as well as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Air_Madagascar" title="Air Madagascar">\n        Air Madagascar\n       </a>\n       logo.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:OaklandZooLemurs.jpg">\n         <img alt="Two ring-tailed lemurs curled up together" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="599" data-file-width="899" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/OaklandZooLemurs.jpg/220px-OaklandZooLemurs.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/OaklandZooLemurs.jpg/330px-OaklandZooLemurs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/OaklandZooLemurs.jpg/440px-OaklandZooLemurs.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:OaklandZooLemurs.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The\n         <a href="/wiki/Ring-tailed_lemur" title="Ring-tailed lemur">\n          ring-tailed lemur\n         </a>\n         is one of over 100 known species and subspecies of lemur found only in Madagascar.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2009Mittermeier_44-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-2009Mittermeier-44">\n           [44]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Like its flora, Madagascar\'s fauna is diverse and exhibits a high rate of endemism. Lemurs have been characterized as "Madagascar\'s flagship mammal species" by Conservation International.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIHotSpot_23-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CIHotSpot-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the absence of\n       <a href="/wiki/Monkey" title="Monkey">\n        monkeys\n       </a>\n       and other competitors, these\n       <a href="/wiki/Primate" title="Primate">\n        primates\n       </a>\n       have adapted to a wide range of habitats and diversified into numerous species. As of 2012\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , there were officially\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_lemur_species" title="List of lemur species">\n        103 species and subspecies of lemur\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lemurextinction_45-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-lemurextinction-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       39 of which were described by zoologists between 2000 and 2008.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mittermeier2008_46-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Mittermeier2008-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       They are almost all classified as rare, vulnerable, or endangered. At least 17 species of lemur have become extinct since humans arrived on Madagascar, all of which were larger than the surviving lemur species.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A number of other mammals, including the cat-like\n       <a href="/wiki/Fossa_(animal)" title="Fossa (animal)">\n        fossa\n       </a>\n       , are endemic to Madagascar. Over 300 species of birds have been recorded on the island, of which over 60\xc2\xa0percent (including four families and 42 genera) are endemic.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIHotSpot_23-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CIHotSpot-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The few families and genera of\n       <a href="/wiki/Reptile" title="Reptile">\n        reptile\n       </a>\n       that have reached Madagascar have diversified into more than 260 species, with over 90\xc2\xa0percent of these being endemic\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Okajima_48-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Okajima-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       (including one endemic family).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIHotSpot_23-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CIHotSpot-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The island is home to two-thirds of the world\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Chameleon" title="Chameleon">\n        chameleon\n       </a>\n       species,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Okajima_48-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Okajima-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       including the\n       <a href="/wiki/Brookesia_micra" title="Brookesia micra">\n        smallest known\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n        <a href="#cite_note-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and researchers have proposed that Madagascar may be the origin of all chameleons.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Endemic fish of Madagascar include two families, 15 genera and over 100 species, primarily inhabiting the island\'s freshwater lakes and rivers. Although invertebrates remain poorly studied on Madagascar, researchers have found high rates of endemism among the known species. All 651 species of terrestrial snail are endemic, as are a majority of the island\'s butterflies,\n       <a href="/wiki/Scarabaeidae" title="Scarabaeidae">\n        scarab beetles\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lacewing" title="Lacewing">\n        lacewings\n       </a>\n       , spiders and dragonflies.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIHotSpot_23-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CIHotSpot-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_issues">\n        Environmental issues\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Environmental issues">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/Deforestation_in_Madagascar" title="Deforestation in Madagascar">\n        Deforestation in Madagascar\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Illegal_logging_in_Madagascar" title="Illegal logging in Madagascar">\n        Illegal logging in Madagascar\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:612px;max-width:612px">\n        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Manantenina_bushfire.jpg">\n           <img alt="Burning Malagasy rainforest" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Manantenina_bushfire.jpg/200px-Manantenina_bushfire.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Manantenina_bushfire.jpg/300px-Manantenina_bushfire.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Manantenina_bushfire.jpg/400px-Manantenina_bushfire.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Madagascar_erosion.jpg">\n           <img alt="A vast, red soil gully caused by erosion" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Madagascar_erosion.jpg/200px-Madagascar_erosion.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Madagascar_erosion.jpg/300px-Madagascar_erosion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Madagascar_erosion.jpg/400px-Madagascar_erosion.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bombetoka_Bay,_April_2005.jpg">\n           <img alt="Aerial photograph of a forked river that has turned red due to red soil runoff." data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Bombetoka_Bay%2C_April_2005.jpg/200px-Bombetoka_Bay%2C_April_2005.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Bombetoka_Bay%2C_April_2005.jpg/300px-Bombetoka_Bay%2C_April_2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Bombetoka_Bay%2C_April_2005.jpg/400px-Bombetoka_Bay%2C_April_2005.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div style="clear:left">\n        </div>\n        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">\n         Tavy (\n         <a href="/wiki/Slash-and-burn" title="Slash-and-burn">\n          slash-and-burn\n         </a>\n         ) destruction of native forest habitat is widespread (left), causing massive erosion (center) and silting of rivers (right).\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Madagascar\'s varied fauna and flora are endangered by human activity.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Since the arrival of humans around 2,350\xc2\xa0years ago, Madagascar has lost more than 90\xc2\xa0percent of its original forest.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This forest loss is largely fueled by\n       <i>\n        tavy\n       </i>\n       ("fat"), a traditional\n       <a href="/wiki/Slash-and-burn" title="Slash-and-burn">\n        slash-and-burn\n       </a>\n       agricultural practice imported to Madagascar by the earliest settlers.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gade_1996_52-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Gade_1996-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Malagasy farmers embrace and perpetuate the practice not only for its practical benefits as an agricultural technique, but for its cultural associations with prosperity, health and venerated ancestral custom (\n       <i>\n        fomba malagasy\n       </i>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n        <a href="#cite_note-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As human population density rose on the island, deforestation accelerated beginning around 1400 years ago.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated4_54-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated4-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       By the 16th century, the central highlands had been largely cleared of their original forests.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gade_1996_52-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Gade_1996-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       More recent contributors to the loss of forest cover include the growth in cattle herd size since their introduction around 1000 years ago, a continued reliance on charcoal as a fuel for cooking, and the increased prominence of coffee as a cash crop over the past century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spittingwind_55-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-spittingwind-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       According to a conservative estimate, about 40\xc2\xa0percent of the island\'s original forest cover was lost from the 1950s to 2000, with a thinning of remaining forest areas by 80\xc2\xa0percent.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n        <a href="#cite_note-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In addition to traditional agricultural practice, wildlife conservation is challenged by the illicit harvesting of protected forests, as well as the state-sanctioned harvesting of precious woods within national parks. Although banned by then-President\n       <a href="/wiki/Marc_Ravalomanana" title="Marc Ravalomanana">\n        Marc Ravalomanana\n       </a>\n       from 2000 to 2009, the collection of small quantities of precious timber from national parks was re-authorized in January 2009 and dramatically intensified under the administration of\n       <a href="/wiki/Andry_Rajoelina" title="Andry Rajoelina">\n        Andry Rajoelina\n       </a>\n       as a key source of state revenues to offset cuts in donor support following Ravalomanana\'s ousting.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CrossroadsMarcus_57-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CrossroadsMarcus-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       It is anticipated that all the island\'s rainforests, excluding those in protected areas and the steepest eastern mountain slopes, will have been deforested by 2025.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Invasive species have likewise been introduced by human populations. Following the 2014 discovery in Madagascar of the Asian common toad, a relative of a toad species that has severely harmed wildlife in Australia since the 1930s, researchers warned the toad could "wreak havoc on the country\'s unique fauna."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Habitat destruction and hunting have threatened many of Madagascar\'s endemic species or driven them to extinction. The island\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Elephant_bird" title="Elephant bird">\n        elephant birds\n       </a>\n       , a family of endemic giant\n       <a href="/wiki/Ratite" title="Ratite">\n        ratites\n       </a>\n       , became extinct in the 17th century or earlier, most probably due to human hunting of adult birds and poaching of their large eggs for food.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davies_60-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Davies-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Numerous\n       <a href="/wiki/Subfossil_lemur" title="Subfossil lemur">\n        giant lemur\n       </a>\n       species vanished with the arrival of human settlers to the island, while others became extinct over the course of the centuries as a growing human population put greater pressures on lemur habitats and, among some populations, increased the rate of lemur hunting for food.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A July 2012 assessment found that the exploitation of natural resources since 2009 has had dire consequences for the island\'s wildlife: 90\xc2\xa0percent of lemur species were found to be threatened with extinction, the highest proportion of any mammalian group. Of these, 23 species were classified as critically endangered. By contrast, a previous study in 2008 had found only 38\xc2\xa0percent of lemur species were at risk of extinction.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lemurextinction_45-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-lemurextinction-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2003 Ravalomanana announced the Durban Vision, an initiative to more than triple the island\'s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_parks_of_Madagascar" title="National parks of Madagascar">\n        protected natural areas\n       </a>\n       to over 60,000\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       (23,000\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi) or 10\xc2\xa0percent of Madagascar\'s land surface. As of 2011\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , areas protected by the state included five Strict Nature Reserves (\n       <i>\n        R\xc3\xa9serves Naturelles Int\xc3\xa9grales\n       </i>\n       ), 21 Wildlife Reserves (\n       <i>\n        R\xc3\xa9serves Sp\xc3\xa9ciales\n       </i>\n       ) and 21 National Parks (\n       <i>\n        Parcs Nationaux\n       </i>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2007 six of the national parks were declared a joint\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_Madagascar" title="List of World Heritage Sites in Madagascar">\n        World Heritage Site\n       </a>\n       under the name\n       <a href="/wiki/Rainforests_of_the_Atsinanana" title="Rainforests of the Atsinanana">\n        Rainforests of the Atsinanana\n       </a>\n       . These parks are\n       <a href="/wiki/Marojejy_National_Park" title="Marojejy National Park">\n        Marojejy\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Masoala_National_Park" title="Masoala National Park">\n        Masoala\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ranomafana_National_Park" title="Ranomafana National Park">\n        Ranomafana\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Zahamena_National_Park" title="Zahamena National Park">\n        Zahamena\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Andohahela_National_Park" title="Andohahela National Park">\n        Andohahela\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Andringitra_National_Park" title="Andringitra National Park">\n        Andringitra\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n        <a href="#cite_note-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Local timber merchants are harvesting scarce species of rosewood trees from protected rainforests within Marojejy National Park and exporting the wood to China for the production of luxury furniture and musical instruments.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">\n        <a href="#cite_note-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       To raise public awareness of Madagascar\'s environmental challenges, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_Conservation_Society" title="Wildlife Conservation Society">\n        Wildlife Conservation Society\n       </a>\n       opened an exhibit entitled "\n       <i>\n        Madagascar!\n       </i>\n       " in June 2008 at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Bronx_Zoo" title="Bronx Zoo">\n        Bronx Zoo\n       </a>\n       in New York.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n        <a href="#cite_note-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Madagascar" title="History of Madagascar">\n        History of Madagascar\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_period">\n        Early period\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Early period">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Malagasy_girls_Madagascar_Merina.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Malagasy_girls_Madagascar_Merina.jpg/220px-Malagasy_girls_Madagascar_Merina.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Malagasy_girls_Madagascar_Merina.jpg/330px-Malagasy_girls_Madagascar_Merina.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Malagasy_girls_Madagascar_Merina.jpg/440px-Malagasy_girls_Madagascar_Merina.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Malagasy_girls_Madagascar_Merina.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_people" title="Malagasy people">\n          Malagasy\n         </a>\n         ancestry reflects a blend of Austronesian (Southeast Asian) and Bantu (East African) roots.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The settlement of Madagascar is a subject of ongoing research and debate.\n       <a href="/wiki/Archaeology" title="Archaeology">\n        Archaeological\n       </a>\n       finds such as cut marks on bones found in the northwest and stone tools in the northeast indicate that Madagascar was visited by foragers around 2000\xc2\xa0BC.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">\n        <a href="#cite_note-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">\n        <a href="#cite_note-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Traditionally, archaeologists have estimated that the earliest settlers arrived in successive waves throughout the period between 350\xc2\xa0BC and 550\xc2\xa0AD, while others are cautious about dates earlier than 250\xc2\xa0AD. In either case, these dates make Madagascar one of the last major landmasses on Earth to be settled by humans.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n        <a href="#cite_note-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Early settlers arrived in\n       <a href="/wiki/Outrigger_canoe" title="Outrigger canoe">\n        outrigger canoes\n       </a>\n       from southern\n       <a href="/wiki/Borneo" title="Borneo">\n        Borneo\n       </a>\n       . Upon arrival, early settlers practiced slash-and-burn agriculture to clear the coastal\n       <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">\n        rainforests\n       </a>\n       for cultivation. The first settlers encountered Madagascar\'s abundance of megafauna, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Subfossil_lemur" title="Subfossil lemur">\n        giant lemurs\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Elephant_bird" title="Elephant bird">\n        elephant birds\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Giant_fossa" title="Giant fossa">\n        giant fossa\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_hippopotamus" title="Malagasy hippopotamus">\n        Malagasy hippopotamus\n       </a>\n       , which have since become extinct due to hunting and habitat destruction.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n        <a href="#cite_note-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       By 600\xc2\xa0AD groups of these early settlers had begun clearing the forests of the central highlands.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Camp93_70-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Camp93-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab" title="Arab">\n        Arab\n       </a>\n       traders first reached the island between the seventh and ninth centuries.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wink_71-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Wink-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A wave of\n       <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">\n        Bantu\n       </a>\n       -speaking migrants from southeastern Africa arrived around 1000\xc2\xa0AD. They introduced the\n       <a href="/wiki/Zebu" title="Zebu">\n        zebu\n       </a>\n       , a type of long-horned humped cattle, which they kept in large herds.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gade_1996_52-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Gade_1996-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       By 1600, irrigated paddy fields were developed in the central highland\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Betsileo" title="Betsileo">\n        Betsileo\n       </a>\n       Kingdom, and were extended with terraced paddies throughout the neighboring Kingdom of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imerina" title="Imerina">\n        Imerina\n       </a>\n       a century later.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Camp93_70-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Camp93-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The rising intensity of land cultivation and the ever-increasing demand for zebu pasturage had largely transformed the central highlands from a forest ecosystem to grassland by the 17th century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gade_1996_52-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Gade_1996-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The oral histories of the Merina people, who may have arrived in the central highlands between 600 and 1000 years ago, describe encountering an established population they called the\n       <a href="/wiki/Vazimba" title="Vazimba">\n        Vazimba\n       </a>\n       . Probably the descendants of an earlier and less technologically advanced Austronesian settlement wave, the Vazimba were assimilated or expelled from the highlands by the Merina kings\n       <a href="/wiki/Andriamanelo" title="Andriamanelo">\n        Andriamanelo\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ralambo" title="Ralambo">\n        Ralambo\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Andrianjaka" title="Andrianjaka">\n        Andrianjaka\n       </a>\n       in the 16th and early 17th centuries.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vazimbadjp_72-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-vazimbadjp-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Today, the spirits of the Vazimba are revered as\n       <i>\n        tompontany\n       </i>\n       (ancestral masters of the land) by many traditional Malagasy communities.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mythe_73-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Mythe-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Arab_and_European_contacts">\n        Arab and European contacts\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Arab and European contacts">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pirates_Cemetery_Ile_Ste_Marie_Madagascar.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Pirates_Cemetery_Ile_Ste_Marie_Madagascar.jpg/220px-Pirates_Cemetery_Ile_Ste_Marie_Madagascar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Pirates_Cemetery_Ile_Ste_Marie_Madagascar.jpg/330px-Pirates_Cemetery_Ile_Ste_Marie_Madagascar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Pirates_Cemetery_Ile_Ste_Marie_Madagascar.jpg/440px-Pirates_Cemetery_Ile_Ste_Marie_Madagascar.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pirates_Cemetery_Ile_Ste_Marie_Madagascar.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A pirate cemetery at\n         <a href="/wiki/%C3%8Ele_Sainte-Marie" title="\xc3\x8ele Sainte-Marie">\n          \xc3\x8ele Sainte-Marie\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Madagascar was an important transoceanic trading hub connecting ports of the Indian Ocean in the early centuries following human settlement.
