The\n       <a href="/wiki/Recorded_history" title="Recorded history">\n        written history\n       </a>\n       of Madagascar began with the Arabs, who established trading posts along the northwest coast by at least the 10th century and introduced\n       <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">\n        Islam\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Arabic_script" title="Arabic script">\n        Arabic script\n       </a>\n       (used to transcribe the Malagasy language in a form of writing known as\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sorabe" title="Sorabe">\n         sorabe\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ), Arab astrology, and other cultural elements.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_20-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LOC-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       European contact began in 1500, when the\n       <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">\n        Portuguese\n       </a>\n       sea captain\n       <a href="/wiki/Diogo_Dias" title="Diogo Dias">\n        Diogo Dias\n       </a>\n       sighted the island.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BGNote_14-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BGNote-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The French established trading posts along the east coast in the late 17th century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_20-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LOC-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       From about 1774 to 1824, Madagascar gained prominence among pirates and European traders, particularly those involved in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">\n        trans-Atlantic slave trade\n       </a>\n       . The small island of\n       <a href="/wiki/%C3%8Ele_Sainte-Marie" title="\xc3\x8ele Sainte-Marie">\n        Nosy Boroha\n       </a>\n       off the northeastern coast of Madagascar has been proposed by some historians as the site of the legendary pirate utopia of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Libertalia" title="Libertalia">\n        Libertalia\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n        <a href="#cite_note-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Many European sailors were shipwrecked on the coasts of the island, among them\n       <a href="/wiki/Robert_Drury_(sailor)" title="Robert Drury (sailor)">\n        Robert Drury\n       </a>\n       , whose journal is one of the few written depictions of life in southern Madagascar during the 18th century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">\n        <a href="#cite_note-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The wealth generated by maritime trade spurred the rise of organized kingdoms on the island, some of which had grown quite powerful by the 17th century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">\n        <a href="#cite_note-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Among these were the\n       <a href="/wiki/Betsimisaraka_people" title="Betsimisaraka people">\n        Betsimisaraka\n       </a>\n       alliance of the eastern coast and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sakalava" title="Sakalava">\n        Sakalava\n       </a>\n       chiefdoms of\n       <a href="/wiki/Menabe" title="Menabe">\n        Menabe\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Boina_Kingdom" title="Boina Kingdom">\n        Boina\n       </a>\n       on the west coast. The Kingdom of Imerina, located in the central highlands with its capital at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Rova_of_Antananarivo" title="Rova of Antananarivo">\n        royal palace\n       </a>\n       of Antananarivo, emerged at around the same time under the leadership of King Andriamanelo.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ogot_77-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Ogot-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdom_of_Madagascar">\n        Kingdom of Madagascar\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Kingdom of Madagascar">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Merina_Kingdom" title="Merina Kingdom">\n        Merina Kingdom\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Andrianampoinimerina.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="495" data-file-width="398" height="211" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Andrianampoinimerina.jpg/170px-Andrianampoinimerina.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Andrianampoinimerina.jpg/255px-Andrianampoinimerina.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Andrianampoinimerina.jpg/340px-Andrianampoinimerina.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Andrianampoinimerina.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         King\n         <a href="/wiki/Andrianampoinimerina" title="Andrianampoinimerina">\n          Andrianampoinimerina\n         </a>\n         (1787\xe2\x80\x931810)\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Upon its emergence in the early 17th century, the highland kingdom of Imerina was initially a minor power relative to the larger coastal kingdoms\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ogot_77-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Ogot-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and grew even weaker in the early 18th century when King\n       <a href="/wiki/Andriamasinavalona" title="Andriamasinavalona">\n        Andriamasinavalona\n       </a>\n       divided it among his four sons. Following almost a century of warring and famine, Imerina was reunited in 1793 by King\n       <a href="/wiki/Andrianampoinimerina" title="Andrianampoinimerina">\n        Andrianampoinimerina\n       </a>\n       (1787\xe2\x80\x931810).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hodder_78-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Hodder-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       From his initial capital\n       <a href="/wiki/Ambohimanga" title="Ambohimanga">\n        Ambohimanga\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">\n        <a href="#cite_note-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and later from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Rova_of_Antananarivo" title="Rova of Antananarivo">\n        Rova of Antananarivo\n       </a>\n       , this Merina king rapidly expanded his rule over neighboring principalities. His ambition to bring the entire island under his control was largely achieved by his son and successor, King\n       <a href="/wiki/Radama_I" title="Radama I">\n        Radama I\n       </a>\n       (1810\xe2\x80\x9328), who was recognized by the British government as King of Madagascar. Radama concluded a treaty in 1817 with the British governor of\n       <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">\n        Mauritius\n       </a>\n       to abolish the lucrative slave trade in return for British military and financial assistance. Artisan missionary envoys from the\n       <a href="/wiki/London_Missionary_Society" title="London Missionary Society">\n        London Missionary Society\n       </a>\n       began arriving in 1818 and included such key figures as\n       <a href="/wiki/James_Cameron_(missionary)" title="James Cameron (missionary)">\n        James Cameron\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/David_Jones_(missionary)" title="David Jones (missionary)">\n        David Jones\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/David_Griffiths_(missionary)" title="David Griffiths (missionary)">\n        David Griffiths\n       </a>\n       , who established schools, transcribed the\n       <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_language" title="Malagasy language">\n        Malagasy language\n       </a>\n       using the\n       <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">\n        Roman alphabet\n       </a>\n       , translated the Bible, and introduced a variety of new technologies to the island.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ade_Ajayi_1998.2C_pp._413.E2.80.93422_80-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Ade_Ajayi_1998.2C_pp._413.E2.80.93422-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Radama\'s successor, Queen\n       <a href="/wiki/Ranavalona_I" title="Ranavalona I">\n        Ranavalona I\n       </a>\n       (1828\xe2\x80\x9361), responded to increasing political and cultural encroachment on the part of Britain and France by issuing a royal edict prohibiting the practice of\n       <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Madagascar" title="Christianity in Madagascar">\n        Christianity in Madagascar\n       </a>\n       and pressuring most foreigners to leave the territory. Residents of Madagascar could accuse one another of various crimes, including theft, Christianity and especially witchcraft, for which the ordeal of\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Tangena" title="Tangena">\n         tangena\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       was routinely obligatory. Between 1828 and 1861, the\n       <i>\n        tangena\n       </i>\n       ordeal caused about 3,000 deaths annually.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">\n        <a href="#cite_note-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Among those who continued to reside in Imerina were\n       <a href="/wiki/Jean_Laborde" title="Jean Laborde">\n        Jean Laborde\n       </a>\n       , an entrepreneur who developed munitions and other industries on behalf of the monarchy, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Joseph-Fran%C3%A7ois_Lambert" title="Joseph-Fran\xc3\xa7ois Lambert">\n        Joseph-Fran\xc3\xa7ois Lambert\n       </a>\n       , a French adventurer and slave trader, with whom then-Prince\n       <a href="/wiki/Radama_II" title="Radama II">\n        Radama II\n       </a>\n       signed a controversial trade agreement termed the Lambert Charter. Succeeding his mother, Radama II (1861\xe2\x80\x9363) attempted to relax the queen\'s stringent policies, but was\n       <a href="/wiki/Radama_II#Assassination_plot" title="Radama II">\n        overthrown\n       </a>\n       two years later by Prime Minister\n       <a href="/wiki/Rainivoninahitriniony" title="Rainivoninahitriniony">\n        Rainivoninahitriniony\n       </a>\n       (1852\xe2\x80\x931865) and an alliance of\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Andriana" title="Andriana">\n         Andriana\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (noble) and\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Hova_(Madagascar)" title="Hova (Madagascar)">\n         Hova\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (commoner) courtiers, who sought to end the absolute power of the monarch.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_20-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LOC-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Following the coup, the courtiers offered Radama\'s queen\n       <a href="/wiki/Rasoherina" title="Rasoherina">\n        Rasoherina\n       </a>\n       (1863\xe2\x80\x9368) the opportunity to rule, if she would accept a power sharing arrangement with the Prime Minister\xe2\x80\x94a new social contract that would be sealed by a political marriage between them.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">\n        <a href="#cite_note-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Queen Rasoherina accepted, first wedding Rainivoninahitriniony, then later deposing him and wedding his brother, Prime Minister\n       <a href="/wiki/Rainilaiarivony" title="Rainilaiarivony">\n        Rainilaiarivony\n       </a>\n       (1864\xe2\x80\x9395), who would go on to marry Queen\n       <a href="/wiki/Ranavalona_II" title="Ranavalona II">\n        Ranavalona II\n       </a>\n       (1868\xe2\x80\x9383) and Queen\n       <a href="/wiki/Ranavalona_III" title="Ranavalona III">\n        Ranavalona III\n       </a>\n       (1883\xe2\x80\x9397) in succession.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">\n        <a href="#cite_note-83">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Over the course of Rainilaiarivony\'s 31-year tenure as prime minister, numerous policies were adopted to modernize and consolidate the power of the central government.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TA910_84-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-TA910-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Schools were constructed throughout the island and attendance was made mandatory. Army organization was improved, and British consultants were employed to train and professionalize soldiers.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FFO522_85-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FFO522-85">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Polygamy" title="Polygamy">\n        Polygamy\n       </a>\n       was outlawed and Christianity, declared the official religion of the court in 1869, was adopted alongside traditional beliefs among a growing portion of the populace.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TA910_84-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-TA910-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Legal codes were reformed on the basis of British\n       <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">\n        common law\n       </a>\n       and three European-style courts were established in the capital city.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FFO522_85-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FFO522-85">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In his joint role as Commander-in-Chief, Rainilaiarivony also successfully ensured the defense of Madagascar against several French colonial incursions.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FFO522_85-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FFO522-85">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="French_colonization">\n        French colonization\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: French colonization">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_Protectorate" title="Malagasy Protectorate">\n        Malagasy Protectorate\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/French_Madagascar" title="French Madagascar">\n        French Madagascar\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LaGuerreAMadagascar.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1370" data-file-width="934" height="323" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/LaGuerreAMadagascar.jpg/220px-LaGuerreAMadagascar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/LaGuerreAMadagascar.jpg/330px-LaGuerreAMadagascar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/LaGuerreAMadagascar.jpg/440px-LaGuerreAMadagascar.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LaGuerreAMadagascar.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A French poster about the\n         <a href="/wiki/Franco-Hova_Wars" title="Franco-Hova Wars">\n          Franco-Hova War\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Colonie_de_Madagascar_1897.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3493" data-file-width="4981" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Colonie_de_Madagascar_1897.jpg/220px-Colonie_de_Madagascar_1897.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Colonie_de_Madagascar_1897.jpg/330px-Colonie_de_Madagascar_1897.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Colonie_de_Madagascar_1897.jpg/440px-Colonie_de_Madagascar_1897.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Colonie_de_Madagascar_1897.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Bond of the french colony Madagascar, issued 7. May 1897\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Primarily on the basis that the Lambert Charter had not been respected, France invaded Madagascar in 1883 in what became known as the first\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Franco-Hova_War" title="Franco-Hova War">\n        Franco-Hova War\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boogaerde_p7_86-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Boogaerde_p7-86">\n         [86]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       At the end of the war, Madagascar ceded the northern port town of\n       <a href="/wiki/Antsiranana" title="Antsiranana">\n        Antsiranana\n       </a>\n       (Diego Suarez) to France and paid 560,000 francs to Lambert\'s heirs.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Randier_p400_87-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Randier_p400-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 1890, the British accepted the full formal imposition of a French\n       <a href="/wiki/Protectorate" title="Protectorate">\n        protectorate\n       </a>\n       on the island, but French authority was not acknowledged by the government of Madagascar. To force capitulation, the French bombarded and occupied the harbor of\n       <a href="/wiki/Toamasina" title="Toamasina">\n        Toamasina\n       </a>\n       on the east coast, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Mahajanga" title="Mahajanga">\n        Mahajanga\n       </a>\n       on the west coast, in December 1894 and January 1895 respectively.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disease_88-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Disease-88">\n         [88]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A French military\n       <a href="/wiki/Flying_column" title="Flying column">\n        flying column\n       </a>\n       then marched toward Antananarivo, losing many men to malaria and other diseases. Reinforcements came from\n       <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">\n        Algeria\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">\n        Sub-Saharan Africa\n       </a>\n       . Upon reaching the city in September 1895, the column bombarded the royal palace with heavy artillery, causing heavy casualties and leading Queen Ranavalona III to surrender.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">\n        <a href="#cite_note-89">\n         [89]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       France annexed Madagascar in 1896 and declared the island a colony the following year, dissolving the Merina monarchy and sending the royal family into exile on\n       <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="R\xc3\xa9union">\n        R\xc3\xa9union Island\n       </a>\n       and to Algeria. A two-year\n       <a href="/wiki/Menalamba_rebellion" title="Menalamba rebellion">\n        resistance movement\n       </a>\n       organized in response to the French capture of the royal palace was effectively put down at the end of 1897.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">\n        <a href="#cite_note-90">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Under colonial rule, plantations were established for the production of a variety of export crops.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">\n        <a href="#cite_note-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">\n        Slavery\n       </a>\n       was abolished in 1896 and approximately 500,000 slaves were freed; many remained in their former masters\' homes as servants\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">\n        <a href="#cite_note-92">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       or as sharecroppers; in many parts of the island strong discriminatory views against slave descendants are still held today.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">\n        <a href="#cite_note-93">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Wide paved boulevards and gathering places were constructed in the capital city of Antananarivo\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">\n        <a href="#cite_note-94">\n         [94]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the Rova palace compound was turned into a museum.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fr.C3.A9migacci_95-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Fr.C3.A9migacci-95">\n         [95]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Additional schools were built, particularly in rural and coastal areas where the schools of the Merina had not reached. Education became mandatory between the ages of 6 to 13 and focused primarily on French language and practical skills.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">\n        <a href="#cite_note-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Merina royal tradition of\n       <a href="/wiki/Corv%C3%A9e" title="Corv\xc3\xa9e">\n        taxes paid in the form of labor\n       </a>\n       was continued under the French and used to construct a railway and roads linking key coastal cities to Antananarivo.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">\n        <a href="#cite_note-97">\n         [97]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Malagasy troops fought for France in\n       <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">\n        World War I\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BGNote_14-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BGNote-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the 1930s,\n       <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">\n        Nazi\n       </a>\n       political thinkers developed the\n       <a href="/wiki/Madagascar_Plan" title="Madagascar Plan">\n        Madagascar Plan\n       </a>\n       that had identified the island as a potential site for the deportation of Europe\'s Jews.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-contemplation_98-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-contemplation-98">\n         [98]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       During the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War">\n        Second World War\n       </a>\n       , the island was the site of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Madagascar" title="Battle of Madagascar">\n        Battle of Madagascar\n       </a>\n       between the\n       <a href="/wiki/Vichy_France" title="Vichy France">\n        Vichy government\n       </a>\n       and the British.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">\n        <a href="#cite_note-99">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The occupation of France during the Second World War tarnished the prestige of the colonial administration in Madagascar and galvanized the growing independence movement, leading to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_Uprising" title="Malagasy Uprising">\n        Malagasy Uprising\n       </a>\n       of 1947.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">\n        <a href="#cite_note-100">\n         [100]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This movement led the French to establish reformed institutions in 1956 under the\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loi_Cadre" title="Loi Cadre">\n         Loi Cadre\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (Overseas Reform Act), and Madagascar moved peacefully towards independence.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kitchen_1962.2C_p._256_101-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Kitchen_1962.2C_p._256-101">\n         [101]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_Republic" title="Malagasy Republic">\n        Malagasy Republic\n       </a>\n       was proclaimed on 14 October 1958, as an\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autonomous_entity" title="Autonomous entity">\n        autonomous\n       </a>\n       state within the\n       <a href="/wiki/French_Community" title="French Community">\n        French Community\n       </a>\n       . A period of provisional government ended with the adoption of a constitution in 1959 and full independence on 26 June 1960.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">\n        <a href="#cite_note-102">\n         [102]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Independent_state">\n        Independent state\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Independent state">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_Republic" title="Malagasy Republic">\n        Malagasy Republic\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Madagascar" title="Democratic Republic of Madagascar">\n        Democratic Republic of Madagascar\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Third_Republic_of_Madagascar" title="Third Republic of Madagascar">\n        Third Republic of Madagascar\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F013783-0033,_Berlin,_Staatsbesuch_aus_Madagaskar-2.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="705" data-file-width="531" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F013783-0033%2C_Berlin%2C_Staatsbesuch_aus_Madagaskar-2.jpg/170px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F013783-0033%2C_Berlin%2C_Staatsbesuch_aus_Madagaskar-2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F013783-0033%2C_Berlin%2C_Staatsbesuch_aus_Madagaskar-2.jpg/255px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F013783-0033%2C_Berlin%2C_Staatsbesuch_aus_Madagaskar-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F013783-0033%2C_Berlin%2C_Staatsbesuch_aus_Madagaskar-2.jpg/340px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F013783-0033%2C_Berlin%2C_Staatsbesuch_aus_Madagaskar-2.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F013783-0033,_Berlin,_Staatsbesuch_aus_Madagaskar-2.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Philibert_Tsiranana" title="Philibert Tsiranana">\n          Philibert Tsiranana\n         </a>\n         , the first\n         <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_Madagascar" title="List of Presidents of Madagascar">\n          president of Madagascar\n         </a>\n         (1960\xe2\x80\x9372).\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Since regaining independence, Madagascar has transitioned through four republics with corresponding revisions to its constitution. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_Republic" title="Malagasy Republic">\n        First Republic\n       </a>\n       (1960\xe2\x80\x9372), under the leadership of French-appointed President\n       <a href="/wiki/Philibert_Tsiranana" title="Philibert Tsiranana">\n        Philibert Tsiranana\n       </a>\n       , was characterized by a continuation of strong economic and political ties to France. Many high-level technical positions were filled by French expatriates, and French teachers, textbooks and curricula continued to be used in schools around the country. Popular resentment over Tsiranana\'s tolerance for this "neo-colonial" arrangement inspired a\n       <a href="/wiki/Rotaka" title="Rotaka">\n        series of farmer and student protests\n       </a>\n       that overturned his administration in 1972.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_20-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LOC-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_Ramanantsoa" title="Gabriel Ramanantsoa">\n        Gabriel Ramanantsoa\n       </a>\n       , a major general in the army, was appointed interim president and prime minister that same year, but low public approval forced him to step down in 1975. Colonel\n       <a href="/wiki/Richard_Ratsimandrava" title="Richard Ratsimandrava">\n        Richard Ratsimandrava\n       </a>\n       , appointed to succeed him, was assassinated six days into his tenure. General\n       <a href="/wiki/Gilles_Andriamahazo" title="Gilles Andriamahazo">\n        Gilles Andriamahazo\n       </a>\n       ruled after Ratsimandrava for four months before being replaced by another military appointee: Vice Admiral\n       <a href="/wiki/Didier_Ratsiraka" title="Didier Ratsiraka">\n        Didier Ratsiraka\n       </a>\n       , who ushered in the socialist-Marxist\n       <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Madagascar" title="Democratic Republic of Madagascar">\n        Second Republic\n       </a>\n       that ran under his tenure from 1975 to 1993.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       This period saw a political alignment with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">\n        Eastern Bloc\n       </a>\n       countries and a shift toward economic insularity. These policies, coupled with economic pressures stemming from the\n       <a href="/wiki/1973_oil_crisis" title="1973 oil crisis">\n        1973 oil crisis\n       </a>\n       , resulted in the rapid collapse of Madagascar\'s economy and a sharp decline in living standards,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_20-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LOC-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the country had become completely bankrupt by 1979. The Ratsiraka administration accepted the conditions of transparency, anti-corruption measures and free market policies imposed by the International Monetary Fund, World Bank and various bilateral donors in exchange for their bailout of the nation\'s broken economy.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISS_103-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ISS-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Ratsiraka\'s dwindling popularity in the late 1980s reached a critical point in 1991 when presidential guards opened fire on unarmed protesters during a rally. Within two months, a transitional government had been established under the leadership of\n       <a href="/wiki/Albert_Zafy" title="Albert Zafy">\n        Albert Zafy\n       </a>\n       (1993\xe2\x80\x9396), who went on to win the 1992 presidential elections and inaugurate the\n       <a href="/wiki/Third_Republic_of_Madagascar" title="Third Republic of Madagascar">\n        Third Republic\n       </a>\n       (1992\xe2\x80\x932010).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crisisgroup_104-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-crisisgroup-104">\n         [104]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The new\n       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Madagascar" title="Constitution of Madagascar">\n        Madagascar constitution\n       </a>\n       established a multi-party democracy and a separation of powers that placed significant control in the hands of the National Assembly. The new constitution also emphasized human rights, social and political freedoms, and free trade.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_20-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LOC-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Zafy\'s term, however, was marred by economic decline, allegations of corruption, and his introduction of legislation to give himself greater powers. He was consequently impeached in 1996, and an interim president,\n       <a href="/wiki/Norbert_Ratsirahonana" title="Norbert Ratsirahonana">\n        Norbert Ratsirahonana\n       </a>\n       , was appointed for the three months prior to the next presidential election. Ratsiraka was then voted back into power on a platform of decentralization and economic reforms for a second term which lasted from 1996 to 2001.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISS_103-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ISS-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The contested\n       <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_presidential_election,_2001" title="Malagasy presidential election, 2001">\n        2001 presidential elections\n       </a>\n       in which then-mayor of Antananarivo, Marc Ravalomanana, eventually emerged victorious, caused a seven-month standoff in 2002 between supporters of Ravalomanana and Ratsiraka. The negative economic impact of the political crisis was gradually overcome by Ravalomanana\'s progressive economic and political policies, which encouraged investments in education and ecotourism, facilitated foreign direct investment, and cultivated trading partnerships both regionally and internationally. National GDP grew at an average rate of 7\xc2\xa0percent per year under his administration. In the later half of his second term, Ravalomanana was criticised by domestic and international observers who accused him of increasing authoritarianism and corruption.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISS_103-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ISS-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Opposition leader and then-mayor of Antananarivo, Andry Rajoelina, led a\n       <a href="/wiki/2009_Malagasy_political_crisis" title="2009 Malagasy political crisis">\n        movement in early 2009\n       </a>\n       in which Ravalomanana was pushed from power in an unconstitutional process widely condemned as a\n       <i>\n        coup d\'\xc3\xa9tat\n       </i>\n       . In March 2009, Rajoelina was declared by the Supreme Court as the President of the\n       <a href="/wiki/High_Transitional_Authority" title="High Transitional Authority">\n        High Transitional Authority\n       </a>\n       , an interim governing body responsible for moving the country toward presidential elections. In 2010, a new constitution was\n       <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_constitutional_referendum,_2010" title="Malagasy constitutional referendum, 2010">\n        adopted by referendum\n       </a>\n       , establishing a Fourth Republic, which sustained the democratic, multi-party structure established in the previous constitution.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crisisgroup_104-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-crisisgroup-104">\n         [104]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Hery_Rajaonarimampianina" title="Hery Rajaonarimampianina">\n        Hery Rajaonarimampianina\n       </a>\n       was declared the winner of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_general_election,_2013" title="Malagasy general election, 2013">\n        2013 presidential election\n       </a>\n       , which the international community deemed fair and transparent.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">\n        <a href="#cite_note-105">\n         [105]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Government">\n        Government\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Government">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Structure">\n        Structure\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Structure">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Government_of_Madagascar" title="Government of Madagascar">\n        Government of Madagascar\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Antananarivo06.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Antananarivo06.jpg/300px-Antananarivo06.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Antananarivo06.jpg/450px-Antananarivo06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Antananarivo06.jpg/600px-Antananarivo06.jpg 2x" width="300"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Antananarivo06.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Antananarivo" title="Antananarivo">\n          Antananarivo\n         </a>\n         is the political and economic capital of Madagascar.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Madagascar is a\n       <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">\n        semi-presidential\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">\n        representative democratic\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Diversity_(politics)" title="Diversity (politics)">\n        multi-party\n       </a>\n       republic, wherein the popularly elected president is the head of state and selects a\n       <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Madagascar" title="Prime Minister of Madagascar">\n        prime minister\n       </a>\n       , who recommends candidates to the president to form his cabinet of ministers. According to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Madagascar" title="Constitution of Madagascar">\n        constitution\n       </a>\n       , executive power is exercised by the government while legislative power is vested in the ministerial cabinet, the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Senate_of_Madagascar" title="Senate of Madagascar">\n        Senate\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Madagascar" title="National Assembly of Madagascar">\n        National Assembly\n       </a>\n       , although in reality these two latter bodies have very little power or legislative role. The constitution establishes independent executive, legislative and judicial branches and mandates a popularly elected president limited to three five-year terms.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BGNote_14-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BGNote-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The public directly elects the president and the 127 members of the National Assembly to five-year terms. All 33 members of the Senate serve six-year terms, with 22 senators elected by local officials and 11 appointed by the president. The last National Assembly election was held on 20 December 2013\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BGNote_14-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BGNote-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the last Senate election was held on 30 December 2015.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">\n        <a href="#cite_note-106">\n         [106]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       At the local level, the island\'s 22 provinces are administered by a governor and provincial council. Provinces are further sub-divided into regions and communes. The judiciary is modeled on the French system, with a High Constitutional Court, High Court of Justice, Supreme Court, Court of Appeals, criminal tribunals, and tribunals of first instance.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-justiceMada_107-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-justiceMada-107">\n         [107]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The courts, which adhere to\n       <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">\n        civil law\n       </a>\n       , lack the capacity to quickly and transparently try the cases in the judicial system, often forcing defendants to pass lengthy pretrial detentions in unsanitary and overcrowded prisons.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediainfo_108-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mediainfo-108">\n         [108]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Antananarivo is the administrative capital and largest city of Madagascar.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BGNote_14-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BGNote-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It is located in the highlands region, near the geographic center of the island. King Andrianjaka founded Antananarivo as the capital of his Imerina Kingdom around 1610 or 1625 upon the site of a captured Vazimba capital on the hilltop of\n       <a href="/wiki/Twelve_sacred_hills_of_Imerina#Hill_of_Analamanga" title="Twelve sacred hills of Imerina">\n        Analamanga\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vazimbadjp_72-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-vazimbadjp-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As Merina dominance expanded over neighboring Malagasy peoples in the early 19th century to establish the Kingdom of Madagascar, Antananarivo became the center of administration for virtually the entire island. In 1896 the French colonizers of Madagascar adopted the Merina capital as their center of colonial administration. The city remained the capital of Madagascar after regaining independence in 1960. In 2017, the capital\'s population was estimated at 1,391,433 inhabitants.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">\n        <a href="#cite_note-109">\n         [109]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The next largest cities are\n       <a href="/wiki/Antsirabe" title="Antsirabe">\n        Antsirabe\n       </a>\n       (500,000),\n       <a href="/wiki/Toamasina" title="Toamasina">\n        Toamasina\n       </a>\n       (450,000) and\n       <a href="/wiki/Mahajanga" title="Mahajanga">\n        Mahajanga\n       </a>\n       (400,000).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BGNote_14-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BGNote-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">\n        Politics\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Politics">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Madagascar" title="Politics of Madagascar">\n        Politics of Madagascar\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Madagascar" title="Foreign relations of Madagascar">\n        Foreign relations of Madagascar\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Madagascar" title="Human rights in Madagascar">\n        Human rights in Madagascar\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Since Madagascar gained independence from France in 1960, the island\'s political transitions have been marked by numerous popular protests, several disputed elections, an impeachment, two military coups and one assassination. The island\'s recurrent political crises are often prolonged, with detrimental effects on the local economy, international relations and Malagasy living standards. The eight-month standoff between incumbent Ratsiraka and challenger Marc Ravalomanana following the 2001 presidential elections cost Madagascar millions of dollars in lost tourism and trade revenue as well as damage to infrastructure, such as bombed bridges and buildings damaged by arson.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">\n        <a href="#cite_note-110">\n         [110]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2009_Malagasy_protests" title="2009 Malagasy protests">\n        A series of protests\n       </a>\n       led by Andry Rajoelina against Ravalomanana in early 2009 became violent, with more than 170 people killed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">\n        <a href="#cite_note-111">\n         [111]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Modern politics in Madagascar are colored by the history of Merina subjugation of coastal communities under their rule in the 19th century. The consequent tension between the highland and coastal populations has periodically flared up into isolated events of violence.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ethnicstrife_112-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ethnicstrife-112">\n         [112]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Madagascar has historically been perceived as being on the margin of mainstream African affairs despite being a founding member of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_African_Unity" title="Organisation of African Unity">\n        Organisation of African Unity\n       </a>\n       , which was established in 1963 and dissolved in 2002 to be replaced by the\n       <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">\n        African Union\n       </a>\n       . Madagascar was not permitted to attend the first African Union summit because of a dispute over the results of the 2001 presidential election, but rejoined the African Union in July 2003 after a 14-month hiatus. Madagascar was again suspended by the African Union in March 2009 following the\n       <a href="/wiki/2009_Malagasy_political_crisis" title="2009 Malagasy political crisis">\n        unconstitutional transfer of executive power\n       </a>\n       to Rajoelina.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">\n        <a href="#cite_note-113">\n         [113]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Madagascar is a member of the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">\n        International Criminal Court\n       </a>\n       with a Bilateral Immunity Agreement of protection for the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_military" title="United States military">\n        United States military\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BGNote_14-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BGNote-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_Madagascar" title="List of diplomatic missions of Madagascar">\n        Eleven countries\n       </a>\n       have established embassies in Madagascar, including France, the United Kingdom, the United States, China and India.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">\n        <a href="#cite_note-114">\n         [114]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Human rights in Madagascar are protected under the constitution and the state is a signatory to numerous international agreements including the\n       <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">\n        Universal Declaration of Human Rights\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_the_Rights_of_the_Child" title="Convention on the Rights of the Child">\n        Convention on the Rights of the Child\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DOS_115-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DOS-115">\n         [115]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Religious, ethnic and sexual minorities are protected under the law. Freedom of association and assembly are also guaranteed under the law, although in practice the denial of permits for public assembly has occasionally been used to impede political demonstrations.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CrossroadsMarcus_57-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CrossroadsMarcus-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DOS_115-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DOS-115">\n         [115]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Torture by security forces is rare and state repression is low relative to other countries with comparably few legal safeguards, although arbitrary arrests and the corruption of military and police officers remain problems. Ravalomanana\'s 2004 creation of BIANCO, an anti-corruption bureau, resulted in reduced corruption among Antananarivo\'s lower-level bureaucrats in particular, although high-level officials have not been prosecuted by the bureau.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CrossroadsMarcus_57-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CrossroadsMarcus-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Security">\n        Security\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Security">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Madagascar" title="Military of Madagascar">\n        Military of Madagascar\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The rise of centralized kingdoms among the Sakalava, Merina and other ethnic groups produced the island\'s first standing armies by the 16th century, initially equipped with spears but later with muskets, cannons and other firearms.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">\n        <a href="#cite_note-116">\n         [116]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       By the early 19th century, the Merina sovereigns of the Kingdom of Madagascar had brought much of the island under their control by mobilizing an army of trained and armed soldiers numbering as high as 30,000.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-army_117-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-army-117">\n         [117]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       French attacks on coastal towns in the later part of the century prompted then-Prime Minister Rainilaiarivony to solicit British assistance to provide training to the Merina monarchy\'s army. Despite the training and leadership provided by British military advisers, the Malagasy army was unable to withstand French weaponry and was forced to surrender following an attack on the royal palace at Antananarivo. Madagascar was declared a colony of France in 1897.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">\n        <a href="#cite_note-118">\n         [118]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The political independence and sovereignty of the Malagasy armed forces, which comprises an army, navy and air force, was restored with independence from France in 1960.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">\n        <a href="#cite_note-119">\n         [119]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Since this time the Malagasy military has never engaged in armed conflict with another state or within its own borders, but has occasionally intervened to restore order during periods of political unrest. Under the socialist Second Republic, Admiral Didier Ratsiraka instated mandatory national armed or civil service for all young citizens regardless of gender, a policy that remained in effect from 1976 to 1991.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">\n        <a href="#cite_note-120">\n         [120]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">\n        <a href="#cite_note-121">\n         [121]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The armed forces are under the direction of the Minister of the Interior\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-justiceMada_107-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-justiceMada-107">\n         [107]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and have remained largely neutral during times of political crisis, as during the protracted standoff between incumbent Ratsiraka and challenger Marc Ravalomanana in the disputed 2001 presidential elections, when the military refused to intervene in favor of either candidate. This tradition was broken in 2009, when a segment of the army defected to the side of Andry Rajoelina, then-mayor of Antananarivo, in support of his attempt to force President Ravalomanana from power.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CrossroadsMarcus_57-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CrossroadsMarcus-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Minister of the Interior is responsible for the national police force, paramilitary force (\n       <i>\n        gendarmerie\n       </i>\n       ) and the secret police.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-justiceMada_107-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-justiceMada-107">\n         [107]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The police and gendarmerie are stationed and administered at the local level. However, in 2009 fewer than a third of all communes had access to the services of these security forces, with most lacking local-level headquarters for either corps.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INSTAT_122-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-INSTAT-122">\n         [122]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Traditional community tribunals, called\n       <i>\n        dina\n       </i>\n       , are presided over by elders and other respected figures and remain a key means by which justice is served in rural areas where state presence is weak. Historically, security has been relatively high across the island.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CrossroadsMarcus_57-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CrossroadsMarcus-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Violent crime rates are low, and criminal activities are predominantly crimes of opportunity such as pickpocketing and petty theft, although child prostitution, human trafficking and the production and sale of marijuana and other illegal drugs are increasing.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-justiceMada_107-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-justiceMada-107">\n         [107]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Budget cuts since 2009 have severely impacted the national police force, producing a steep increase in criminal activity in recent years.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CrossroadsMarcus_57-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CrossroadsMarcus-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">\n        Administrative divisions\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Madagascar" title="Regions of Madagascar">\n        Regions of Madagascar\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Madagascar" title="Districts of Madagascar">\n        Districts of Madagascar\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Regions_of_Madagascar.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1458" data-file-width="803" height="399" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Regions_of_Madagascar.svg/440px-Regions_of_Madagascar.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Regions_of_Madagascar.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A map of\n         <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Madagascar" title="Regions of Madagascar">\n          Madagascar\'s regions\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Madagascar is subdivided into 22 regions (\n       <i>\n        faritra\n       </i>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BGNote_14-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BGNote-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The regions are further subdivided into 119 districts, 1,579 communes, and 17,485\n       <i>\n        fokontany\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INSTAT_122-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-INSTAT-122">\n         [122]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable sortable" style="margin: 1em auto 1em </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="United_Nations_involvement">\n        United Nations involvement\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: United Nations involvement">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Madagascar became a Member State of the United Nations on 20 September 1960, shortly after gaining its independence on 26 June 1960.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">\n        <a href="#cite_note-125">\n         [125]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As of January 2017, 34 police officers from Madagascar are deployed in Haiti as part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Stabilisation_Mission_in_Haiti" title="United Nations Stabilisation Mission in Haiti">\n        United Nations Stabilisation Mission in Haiti\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">\n        <a href="#cite_note-126">\n         [126]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Starting in 2015, under the direction of and with assistance from the UN, the World Food Programme started the Madagascar Country Programme with the two main goals of long-term development/ reconstruction efforts and addressing the food insecurity issues in the southern regions of Madagascar.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_127-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:0-127">\n         [127]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       These goals plan to be accomplished by providing meals for specific schools in rural and urban priority areas and by developing national school feeding policies to increase consistency of nourishment throughout the country. Small and local farmers have also been assisted in increasing both the quantity and quality of their production, as well as improving their crop yield in unfavorable weather conditions.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_127-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:0-127">\n         [127]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">\n        Economy\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Economy">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Madagascar" title="Economy of Madagascar">\n        Economy of Madagascar\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Madagascar" title="Tourism in Madagascar">\n        Tourism in Madagascar\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Madagascar_treemap.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="866" data-file-width="1107" height="274" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Madagascar_treemap.png/350px-Madagascar_treemap.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Madagascar_treemap.png/525px-Madagascar_treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Madagascar_treemap.png/700px-Madagascar_treemap.png 2x" width="350"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Madagascar_treemap.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A proportional representation of Madagascar\'s exports\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NappesNosyKomba.JPG">\n         <img alt="embroidered tablecloths hang on lines from palm trees" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/NappesNosyKomba.JPG/220px-NappesNosyKomba.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/NappesNosyKomba.JPG/330px-NappesNosyKomba.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/NappesNosyKomba.JPG/440px-NappesNosyKomba.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NappesNosyKomba.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Embroidered tablecloths are produced for sale to tourists at Nosy Komba.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       During Madagascar\'s First Republic, France heavily influenced Madagascar\'s economic planning and policy and served as its key trading partner. Key products were cultivated and distributed nationally through producers\' and consumers\' cooperatives. Government initiatives such as a rural development program and state farms were established to boost production of commodities such as rice, coffee, cattle, silk and palm oil. Popular dissatisfaction over these policies was a key factor in launching the socialist-Marxist Second Republic, in which the formerly private bank and insurance industries were nationalized; state monopolies were established for such industries as textiles, cotton and power; and import\xe2\x80\x93export trade and shipping were brought under state control. Madagascar\'s economy quickly deteriorated as exports fell, industrial production dropped by 75\xc2\xa0percent, inflation spiked and government debt increased; the rural population was soon reduced to living at subsistence levels. Over 50\xc2\xa0percent of the nation\'s export revenue was spent on debt servicing.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EBLand_19-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EBLand-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The IMF forced Madagascar\'s government to accept structural adjustment policies and liberalization of the economy when the state became bankrupt in 1982 and state-controlled industries were gradually privatized over the course of the 1980s. The political crisis of 1991 led to the suspension of IMF and World Bank assistance. Conditions for the resumption of aid were not met under Zafy, who tried unsuccessfully to attract other forms of revenue for the State before aid was once again resumed under the interim government established upon Zafy\'s impeachment. The IMF agreed to write off half Madagascar\'s debt in 2004 under the Ravalomanana administration. Having met a set of stringent economic, governance and human rights criteria, Madagascar became the first country to benefit from the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Millennium_Challenge_Account" title="Millennium Challenge Account">\n        Millennium Challenge Account\n       </a>\n       in 2005.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BGNote_14-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BGNote-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Madagascar\'s GDP in 2015 was estimated at 9.98 billion USD, with a per capita GDP of $411.82.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">\n        <a href="#cite_note-128">\n         [128]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">\n        <a href="#cite_note-129">\n         [129]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Approximately 69\xc2\xa0percent of the population lives below the national poverty line threshold of one dollar per day.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">\n        <a href="#cite_note-130">\n         [130]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Over the last five years, the average growth rate has been 2.6% but is expected to have reached 4.1% in 2016, due to public works programs and a growth of the service sector.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">\n        <a href="#cite_note-131">\n         [131]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The agriculture sector constituted 29\xc2\xa0percent of Malagasy GDP in 2011, while manufacturing formed 15\xc2\xa0percent of GDP. Madagascar\'s other sources of growth are tourism, agriculture and the extractive industries.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AEO2011_132-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AEO2011-132">\n         [132]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Tourism focuses on the niche eco-tourism market, capitalizing on Madagascar\'s unique biodiversity, unspoiled natural habitats, national parks and lemur species.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tourismsector_133-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tourismsector-133">\n         [133]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       An estimated 365,000 tourists visited Madagascar in 2008, but the sector declined during the political crisis with 180,000 tourists visiting in 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AEO2011_132-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AEO2011-132">\n         [132]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_resources_and_trade">\n        Natural resources and trade\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Natural resources and trade">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Raffia_animals_created_by_artisans_in_Madagascar.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Raffia_animals_created_by_artisans_in_Madagascar.jpg/220px-Raffia_animals_created_by_artisans_in_Madagascar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Raffia_animals_created_by_artisans_in_Madagascar.jpg/330px-Raffia_animals_created_by_artisans_in_Madagascar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Raffia_animals_created_by_artisans_in_Madagascar.jpg/440px-Raffia_animals_created_by_artisans_in_Madagascar.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Raffia_animals_created_by_artisans_in_Madagascar.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Toy animals made from\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Raffia" title="Raffia">\n          raffia\n         </a>\n         , a native palm\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">\n          <a href="#cite_note-134">\n           [134]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Madagascar\'s natural resources include a variety of unprocessed agricultural and mineral resources. Agriculture (including\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Raffia" title="Raffia">\n        raffia\n       </a>\n       ), fishing and\n       <a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">\n        forestry\n       </a>\n       are mainstays of the economy. Madagascar is the world\'s principal supplier of vanilla, cloves\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">\n        <a href="#cite_note-135">\n         [135]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ylang-ylang" title="Ylang-ylang">\n        ylang-ylang\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gafilo_21-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-gafilo-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Other key agricultural resources include coffee,\n       <a href="/wiki/Lychee" title="Lychee">\n        lychees\n       </a>\n       and shrimp. Key mineral resources include various types of precious and semi-precious stones, and Madagascar currently provides half of the world\'s supply of sapphires, which were discovered near\n       <a href="/wiki/Ilakaka" title="Ilakaka">\n        Ilakaka\n       </a>\n       in the late 1990s.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">\n        <a href="#cite_note-136">\n         [136]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Madagascar has one of the world\'s largest reserves of\n       <a href="/wiki/Ilmenite" title="Ilmenite">\n        ilmenite\n       </a>\n       (titanium ore), as well as important reserves of chromite, coal, iron, cobalt, copper and nickel.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EBLand_19-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EBLand-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Several major projects are underway in the mining,\n       <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">\n        oil\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">\n        gas\n       </a>\n       sectors that are anticipated to give a significant boost to the Malagasy economy. These include such projects as ilmenite and zircon mining from heavy mineral sands near\n       <a href="/wiki/T%C3%B4lanaro" title="T\xc3\xb4lanaro">\n        T\xc3\xb4lanaro\n       </a>\n       by\n       <a href="/wiki/Rio_Tinto_Group" title="Rio Tinto Group">\n        Rio Tinto\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RioTinto_137-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-RioTinto-137">\n         [137]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       extraction of nickel near\n       <a href="/wiki/Moramanga" title="Moramanga">\n        Moramanga\n       </a>\n       and its processing near Toamasina by\n       <a href="/wiki/Sherritt_International" title="Sherritt International">\n        Sherritt International\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">\n        <a href="#cite_note-138">\n         [138]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the development of the giant onshore\n       <a href="/wiki/Heavy_crude_oil" title="Heavy crude oil">\n        heavy oil\n       </a>\n       deposits at\n       <a href="/wiki/Tsimiroro" title="Tsimiroro">\n        Tsimiroro\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Bemolanga" title="Bemolanga">\n        Bemolanga\n       </a>\n       by\n       <a href="/wiki/Madagascar_Oil" title="Madagascar Oil">\n        Madagascar Oil\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">\n        <a href="#cite_note-139">\n         [139]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Exports formed 28\xc2\xa0percent of GDP in 2009.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BGNote_14-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BGNote-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Most of the country\'s export revenue is derived from the textiles industry, fish and shellfish, vanilla, cloves and other foodstuffs.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AEO2011_132-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AEO2011-132">\n         [132]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       France is Madagascar\'s main trading partner, although the United States, Japan and Germany also have strong economic ties to the country.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EBLand_19-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EBLand-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar-U.S._Business_Council&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Madagascar-U.S. Business Council (page does not exist)">\n        Madagascar-U.S. Business Council\n       </a>\n       was formed in May 2003, as a collaboration between\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USAID" title="USAID">\n        USAID\n       </a>\n       and Malagasy artisan producers to support the export of local handicrafts to foreign markets.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-handicrafts_140-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-handicrafts-140">\n         [140]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Imports of such items as foodstuffs, fuel, capital goods, vehicles, consumer goods and electronics consume an estimated 52\xc2\xa0percent of GDP. The main sources of Madagascar\'s imports include China, France, Iran, Mauritius and Hong Kong.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BGNote_14-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BGNote-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure_and_media">\n        Infrastructure and media\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Infrastructure and media">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Madagascar" title="Transport in Madagascar">\n        Transport in Madagascar\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Madagascar" title="Telecommunications in Madagascar">\n        Telecommunications in Madagascar\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_newspapers_in_Madagascar" title="List of newspapers in Madagascar">\n        List of newspapers in Madagascar\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Antananarivo_Madagascar_people_reading_news.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3024" data-file-width="4032" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Antananarivo_Madagascar_people_reading_news.JPG/220px-Antananarivo_Madagascar_people_reading_news.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Antananarivo_Madagascar_people_reading_news.JPG/330px-Antananarivo_Madagascar_people_reading_news.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Antananarivo_Madagascar_people_reading_news.JPG/440px-Antananarivo_Madagascar_people_reading_news.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Antananarivo_Madagascar_people_reading_news.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A news stand in Antananarivo\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 2010, Madagascar had approximately 7,617\xc2\xa0km (4,730\xc2\xa0mi) of paved roads, 854\xc2\xa0km (530\xc2\xa0mi) of railways and 432\xc2\xa0km (270\xc2\xa0mi) of navigable waterways.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bradtp2_9-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bradtp2-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The majority of roads in Madagascar are unpaved, with many becoming impassable in the rainy season. Largely paved national routes connect the six largest regional towns to Antananarivo, with minor paved and unpaved routes providing access to other population centers in each district.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_20-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LOC-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There are several rail lines. Antananarivo is connected to Toamasina, Ambatondrazaka and Antsirabe by rail, and another rail line connects Fianarantsoa to Manakara. The most important seaport in Madagascar is located on the east coast at Toamasina. Ports at Mahajanga and Antsiranana are significantly less used due to their remoteness.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_20-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LOC-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The island\'s newest port at Ehoala, constructed in 2008 and privately managed by Rio Tinto, will come under state control upon completion of the company\'s mining project near T\xc3\xb4lanaro around 2038.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RioTinto_137-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-RioTinto-137">\n         [137]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Air Madagascar services the island\'s many small regional airports, which offer the only practical means of access to many of the more remote regions during rainy season road washouts.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_20-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LOC-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Running water and electricity are supplied at the national level by a government service provider,\n       <a href="/wiki/Jirama" title="Jirama">\n        Jirama\n       </a>\n       , which is unable to service the entire population.
