As of 2009\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , only 6.8\xc2\xa0percent of Madagascar\'s\n       <i>\n        fokontany\n       </i>\n       had access to water provided by Jirama, while 9.5\xc2\xa0percent had access to its electricity services.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INSTAT_122-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-INSTAT-122">\n         [122]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       56% of Madagascar\'s power is provided by hydroelectric power plants with the remaining 44% provided by diesel engine generators.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">\n        <a href="#cite_note-141">\n         [141]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Mobile telephone and internet access are widespread in urban areas but remain limited in rural parts of the island. Approximately 30\xc2\xa0percent of the districts are able to access the nations\' several private telecommunications networks via mobile telephones or land lines.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INSTAT_122-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-INSTAT-122">\n         [122]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Radio broadcasts remain the principal means by which the Malagasy population access international, national and local news. Only state radio broadcasts are transmitted across the entire island. Hundreds of public and private stations with local or regional range provide alternatives to state broadcasting.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediainfo_108-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mediainfo-108">\n         [108]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In addition to the state television channel, a variety of privately owned television stations broadcast local and international programming throughout Madagascar. Several media outlets are owned by political partisans or politicians themselves, including the media groups MBS (owned by Ravalomanana) and Viva (owned by Rajoelina),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CrossroadsMarcus_57-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CrossroadsMarcus-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       contributing to political polarization in reporting.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The media has historically come under varying degrees of pressure over time to censor their criticism of the government. Reporters are occasionally threatened or harassed and media outlets are periodically forced to close.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediainfo_108-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mediainfo-108">\n         [108]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Accusations of media censorship have increased since 2009 due to the alleged intensification of restrictions on political criticism.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DOS_115-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DOS-115">\n         [115]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Access to the internet has grown dramatically over the past decade, with an estimated 352,000 residents of Madagascar accessing the internet from home or in one of the nation\'s many internet caf\xc3\xa9s in December 2011.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediainfo_108-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mediainfo-108">\n         [108]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Health">\n        Health\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Health">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Madagascar" title="Healthcare in Madagascar">\n        Healthcare in Madagascar\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Madagascar_woman_with_child.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="683" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Madagascar_woman_with_child.jpg/170px-Madagascar_woman_with_child.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Madagascar_woman_with_child.jpg/255px-Madagascar_woman_with_child.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Madagascar_woman_with_child.jpg/340px-Madagascar_woman_with_child.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Madagascar_woman_with_child.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Maternal mortality declined after 1990 but rose sharply after 2009 due to political instability.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INSTAT_122-4">\n          <a href="#cite_note-INSTAT-122">\n           [122]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Medical centers, dispensaries and hospitals are found throughout the island, although they are concentrated in urban areas and particularly in Antananarivo. Access to medical care remains beyond the reach of many Malagasy, especially in the rural areas, and many recourse to traditional healers.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">\n        <a href="#cite_note-142">\n         [142]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In addition to the high expense of medical care relative to the average Malagasy income, the prevalence of trained medical professionals remains extremely low. In 2010 Madagascar had an average of three hospital beds per 10,000\xc2\xa0people and a total of 3,150\xc2\xa0doctors, 5,661\xc2\xa0nurses, 385\xc2\xa0community health workers, 175\xc2\xa0pharmacists and 57\xc2\xa0dentists for a population of 22\xc2\xa0million. 14.6\xc2\xa0percent of government spending in 2008 was directed toward the health sector. Approximately 70\xc2\xa0percent of spending on health was contributed by the government, while 30\xc2\xa0percent originated with international donors and other private sources.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2011_143-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WHO2011-143">\n         [143]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The government provides at least one basic health center per commune. Private health centers are concentrated within urban areas and particularly those of the central highlands.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INSTAT_122-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-INSTAT-122">\n         [122]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Despite these barriers to access, health services have shown a trend toward improvement over the past twenty years. Child immunizations against such diseases as\n       <a href="/wiki/Hepatitis_B" title="Hepatitis B">\n        hepatitis B\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Diphtheria" title="Diphtheria">\n        diphtheria\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Measles" title="Measles">\n        measles\n       </a>\n       increased an average of 60\xc2\xa0percent in this period, indicating low but increasing availability of basic medical services and treatments. The Malagasy fertility rate in 2009 was 4.6\xc2\xa0children per woman, declining from 6.3 in 1990. Teen pregnancy rates of 14.8\xc2\xa0percent in 2011, much higher than the African average, are a contributing factor to rapid population growth.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2011_143-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WHO2011-143">\n         [143]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2010 the maternal mortality rate was 440 per 100,000 births, compared to 373.1 in 2008 and 484.4 in 1990, indicating a decline in perinatal care following the 2009 coup. The infant mortality rate in 2011 was 41 per 1,000 births,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BGNote_14-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BGNote-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       with an under-five mortality rate at 61 per 1,000 births.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SOWMY_144-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SOWMY-144">\n         [144]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Schistosomiasis" title="Schistosomiasis">\n        Schistosomiasis\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">\n        malaria\n       </a>\n       and sexually transmitted diseases are common in Madagascar, although infection rates of AIDS remain low relative to many countries in mainland Africa, at only 0.2\xc2\xa0percent of the adult population. The malaria mortality rate is also among the lowest in Africa at 8.5 deaths per 100,000\xc2\xa0people, in part due to the highest frequency use of insecticide treated nets in Africa.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2011_143-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WHO2011-143">\n         [143]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Adult life expectancy in 2009 was 63 years for men and 67\xc2\xa0years for women.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2011_143-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WHO2011-143">\n         [143]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2017, Madagascar had an outbreak of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Bubonic_plague" title="Bubonic plague">\n        bubonic plague\n       </a>\n       (also known as the black death) that affected urban areas.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">\n        <a href="#cite_note-145">\n         [145]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">\n        Education\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Education">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Madagascar" title="Education in Madagascar">\n        Education in Madagascar\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Diego_Suarez_Antsiranana_urban_public_primary_school_(EPP)_Madagascar.jpg">\n         <img alt="Students working in groups in classroom as teacher observes" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2386" data-file-width="2916" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Diego_Suarez_Antsiranana_urban_public_primary_school_%28EPP%29_Madagascar.jpg/220px-Diego_Suarez_Antsiranana_urban_public_primary_school_%28EPP%29_Madagascar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Diego_Suarez_Antsiranana_urban_public_primary_school_%28EPP%29_Madagascar.jpg/330px-Diego_Suarez_Antsiranana_urban_public_primary_school_%28EPP%29_Madagascar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Diego_Suarez_Antsiranana_urban_public_primary_school_%28EPP%29_Madagascar.jpg/440px-Diego_Suarez_Antsiranana_urban_public_primary_school_%28EPP%29_Madagascar.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Diego_Suarez_Antsiranana_urban_public_primary_school_(EPP)_Madagascar.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Madagascar" title="Education in Madagascar">\n          Education\n         </a>\n         access and quality were prioritized under\n         <a href="/wiki/Marc_Ravalomanana" title="Marc Ravalomanana">\n          Ravalomanana\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Prior to the 19th century, all education in Madagascar was informal and typically served to teach practical skills as well as social and cultural values, including respect for ancestors and elders.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_20-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LOC-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The first formal European-style school was established in 1818 at\n       <a href="/wiki/Toamasina" title="Toamasina">\n        Toamasina\n       </a>\n       by members of the\n       <a href="/wiki/London_Missionary_Society" title="London Missionary Society">\n        London Missionary Society\n       </a>\n       (LMS). The LMS was invited by King Radama I (1810\xe2\x80\x9328) to expand its schools throughout Imerina to teach basic literacy and numeracy to aristocratic children. The schools were closed by Ranavalona I in 1835\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ralibera_146-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Ralibera-146">\n         [146]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but reopened and expanded in the decades after her death.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       By the end of the 19th century Madagascar had the most developed and modern school system in pre-colonial Sub-Saharan Africa. Access to schooling was expanded in coastal areas during the colonial period, with French language and basic work skills becoming the focus of the curriculum. During the post-colonial First Republic, a continued reliance on French nationals as teachers, and French as the language of instruction, displeased those desiring a complete separation from the former colonial power.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_20-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LOC-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Consequently, under the socialist Second Republic, French instructors and other nationals were expelled, Malagasy was declared the language of instruction and a large cadre of young Malagasy were rapidly trained to teach at remote rural schools under the mandatory two-year national service policy.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">\n        <a href="#cite_note-147">\n         [147]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       This policy, known as\n       <i>\n        malgachization\n       </i>\n       , coincided with a severe economic downturn and a dramatic decline in the quality of education. Those schooled during this period generally failed to master the French language or many other subjects and struggled to find employment, forcing many to take low-paying jobs in the informal or black market that mired them in deepening poverty. Excepting the brief presidency of Albert Zafy, from 1992 to 1996, Ratsiraka remained in power from 1975 to 2001 and failed to achieve significant improvements in education throughout his tenure.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148">\n        <a href="#cite_note-148">\n         [148]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Education was prioritized under the Ravalomanana administration (2002\xe2\x80\x9309), and is currently free and compulsory from ages 6 to 13.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WBeducation_149-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WBeducation-149">\n         [149]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The primary schooling cycle is five years, followed by four years at the lower secondary level and three years at the upper secondary level.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_20-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LOC-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       During Ravalomanana\'s first term, thousands of new primary schools and additional classrooms were constructed, older buildings were renovated, and tens of thousands of new primary teachers were recruited and trained. Primary school fees were eliminated and kits containing basic school supplies were distributed to primary students.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WBeducation_149-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WBeducation-149">\n         [149]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Government school construction initiatives have ensured at least one primary school per\n       <i>\n        fokontany\n       </i>\n       and one lower secondary school within each commune. At least one upper secondary school is located in each of the larger urban centers.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INSTAT_122-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-INSTAT-122">\n         [122]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The three branches of the national public university are located at Antananarivo (founded in 1961), Mahajanga (1977) and Fianarantsoa (1988). These are complemented by public teacher-training colleges and several private universities and technical colleges.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_20-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LOC-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As a result of increased educational access, enrollment rates more than doubled between 1996 and 2006. However, education quality is weak, producing high rates of grade repetition and dropout.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WBeducation_149-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WBeducation-149">\n         [149]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Education policy in Ravalomanana\'s second term focused on quality issues, including an increase in minimum education standards for the recruitment of primary teachers from a middle school leaving certificate (BEPC) to a high school leaving certificate (BAC), and a reformed teacher training program to support the transition from traditional didactic instruction to student-centered teaching methods to boost student learning and participation in the classroom.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150">\n        <a href="#cite_note-150">\n         [150]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Public expenditure on education was 13.4\xc2\xa0percent of total government expenditure and 2.9\xc2\xa0percent of GDP in 2008. Primary classrooms are crowded, with average pupil to teacher ratios of 47:1 in 2008.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">\n        <a href="#cite_note-151">\n         [151]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">\n        Demographics\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Demographics">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Madagascar" title="Demographics of Madagascar">\n        Demographics of Madagascar\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 2016, the population of Madagascar was estimated at 25\xc2\xa0million, up from 2.2 million in 1900.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_5-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_20-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LOC-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The annual population growth rate in Madagascar was approximately 2.9\xc2\xa0percent in 2009.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BGNote_14-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BGNote-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Approximately 42.5\xc2\xa0percent of the population is younger than 15 years of age, while 54.5\xc2\xa0percent are between the ages of 15 and 64. Those aged 65 and older form three percent of the total population.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AEO2011_132-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AEO2011-132">\n         [132]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Only two general censuses, in 1975 and 1993, have been carried out after independence. The most densely populated regions of the island are the eastern highlands and the eastern coast, contrasting most dramatically with the sparsely populated western plains.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_20-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LOC-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">\n        Ethnic groups\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_of_Madagascar" title="Ethnic groups of Madagascar">\n        Ethnic groups of Madagascar\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ethnic_groups_of_Madagascar_Map.png">\n         <img alt="map of Madagascar showing distribution of Malagasy ethnic sub-groups" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="599" data-file-width="471" height="445" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Ethnic_groups_of_Madagascar_Map.png/350px-Ethnic_groups_of_Madagascar_Map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/02/Ethnic_groups_of_Madagascar_Map.png 1.5x" width="350"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ethnic_groups_of_Madagascar_Map.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The regional distribution of\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_of_Madagascar" title="Ethnic groups of Madagascar">\n          Malagasy ethnic sub-groups\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Malagasy ethnic group forms over 90\xc2\xa0percent of Madagascar\'s population and is typically divided into eighteen ethnic sub-groups.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BGNote_14-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BGNote-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Recent DNA research revealed that the genetic makeup of the average Malagasy person constitutes an approximately equal blend of\n       <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">\n        Southeast Asian\n       </a>\n       and East African genes,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152">\n        <a href="#cite_note-152">\n         [152]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tofanelli_153-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Tofanelli-153">\n         [153]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       although the genetics of some communities show a predominance of Southeast Asian or East African origins or some Arab,\n       <a href="/wiki/Indians_in_Madagascar" title="Indians in Madagascar">\n        Indian\n       </a>\n       or European ancestry.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Adelaar_154-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Adelaar-154">\n         [154]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Southeast Asian origins \xe2\x80\x93 specifically from the southern part of Borneo \xe2\x80\x93 are most predominant among the\n       <a href="/wiki/Merina_people" title="Merina people">\n        Merina\n       </a>\n       of the central highlands,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ethnicstrife_112-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ethnicstrife-112">\n         [112]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       who form the largest Malagasy ethnic sub-group at approximately 26\xc2\xa0percent of the population, while certain communities among the coastal peoples (collectively called\n       <i>\n        c\xc3\xb4tiers\n       </i>\n       ) have relatively stronger East African origins. The largest coastal ethnic sub-groups are the\n       <a href="/wiki/Betsimisaraka_people" title="Betsimisaraka people">\n        Betsimisaraka\n       </a>\n       (14.9\xc2\xa0percent) and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tsimihety" title="Tsimihety">\n        Tsimihety\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sakalava" title="Sakalava">\n        Sakalava\n       </a>\n       (6\xc2\xa0percent each).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_20-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LOC-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable" style="margin: 1em auto 1em auto;">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         Malagasy ethnic sub-groups\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Regional concentration\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Antankarana" title="Antankarana">\n          Antankarana\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Sakalava_people" title="Sakalava people">\n          Sakalava\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Tsimihety_people" title="Tsimihety people">\n          Tsimihety\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Former\n         <a href="/wiki/Antsiranana_Province" title="Antsiranana Province">\n          Antsiranana Province\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Sakalava_people" title="Sakalava people">\n          Sakalava\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Vezo_people" title="Vezo people">\n          Vezo\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Former\n         <a href="/wiki/Mahajanga_Province" title="Mahajanga Province">\n          Mahajanga Province\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Betsimisaraka_people" title="Betsimisaraka people">\n          Betsimisaraka\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Sihanaka" title="Sihanaka">\n          Sihanaka\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Bezanozano" title="Bezanozano">\n          Bezanozano\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Former\n         <a href="/wiki/Toamasina_Province" title="Toamasina Province">\n          Toamasina Province\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Merina_people" title="Merina people">\n          Merina\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Former\n         <a href="/wiki/Antananarivo_Province" title="Antananarivo Province">\n          Antananarivo Province\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Betsileo_people" title="Betsileo people">\n          Betsileo\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Antaifasy" title="Antaifasy">\n          Antaifasy\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Antambahoaka" title="Antambahoaka">\n          Antambahoaka\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Antemoro_people" title="Antemoro people">\n          Antaimoro\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Antaisaka_people" title="Antaisaka people">\n          Antaisaka\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Tanala" title="Tanala">\n          Tanala\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Former\n         <a href="/wiki/Fianarantsoa_Province" title="Fianarantsoa Province">\n          Fianarantsoa Province\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Mahafaly" title="Mahafaly">\n          Mahafaly\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Antandroy" title="Antandroy">\n          Antandroy\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Antanosy_people" title="Antanosy people">\n          Antanosy people\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Bara_people" title="Bara people">\n          Bara\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vezo" title="Vezo">\n          Vezo\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Former\n         <a href="/wiki/Toliara_Province" title="Toliara Province">\n          Toliara Province\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people_in_Madagascar" title="Chinese people in Madagascar">\n        Chinese\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Indians_in_Madagascar" title="Indians in Madagascar">\n        Indian\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Comoros" title="Comoros">\n        Comorian\n       </a>\n       minorities are present in Madagascar, as well as a small European (primarily\n       <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">\n        French\n       </a>\n       ) populace. Emigration in the late 20th century has reduced these minority populations, occasionally in abrupt waves, such as the exodus of\n       <a href="/wiki/Comoros" title="Comoros">\n        Comorans\n       </a>\n       in 1976, following anti-Comoran riots in Mahajanga.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_20-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LOC-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       By comparison, there has been no significant emigration of Malagasy peoples.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EBLand_19-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EBLand-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The number of Europeans has declined since independence, reduced from 68,430 in 1958\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kitchen_1962.2C_p._256_101-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Kitchen_1962.2C_p._256-101">\n         [101]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       to 17,000 three decades later. There were an estimated 25,000\xc2\xa0Comorans, 18,000\xc2\xa0Indians, and 9,000\xc2\xa0Chinese living in Madagascar in the mid-1980s.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_20-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LOC-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">\n        Languages\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Languages">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Madagascar_Kids_5_(4814978342).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="1080" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Madagascar_Kids_5_%284814978342%29.jpg/220px-Madagascar_Kids_5_%284814978342%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Madagascar_Kids_5_%284814978342%29.jpg/330px-Madagascar_Kids_5_%284814978342%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Madagascar_Kids_5_%284814978342%29.jpg/440px-Madagascar_Kids_5_%284814978342%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Madagascar_Kids_5_(4814978342).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A Malagasy child\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_language" title="Malagasy language">\n        Malagasy language\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Madagascar" title="Languages of Madagascar">\n        Languages of Madagascar\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Malagasy language is of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malayo-Polynesian" title="Malayo-Polynesian">\n        Malayo-Polynesian\n       </a>\n       origin and is generally spoken throughout the island. The numerous dialects of Malagasy, which are generally mutually intelligible,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">\n        <a href="#cite_note-155">\n         [155]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       can be clustered under one of two sub-groups: eastern Malagasy, spoken along the eastern forests and highlands including the Merina dialect of Antananarivo and western Malagasy, spoken across the western coastal plains. French became the official language during the colonial period, when Madagascar came under the authority of France. In the first national Constitution of 1958, Malagasy and French were named the official languages of the Malagasy Republic. Madagascar is a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francophone" title="Francophone">\n        francophone\n       </a>\n       country, and French is mostly spoken as a second language among the educated population and used for international communication.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_20-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LOC-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       No official languages were recorded in the Constitution of 1992, although Malagasy was identified as the national language. Nonetheless, many sources still claimed that Malagasy and French were official languages, eventually leading a citizen to initiate a legal case against the state in April 2000, on the grounds that the publication of official documents only in the French language was unconstitutional. The High Constitutional Court observed in its decision that, in the absence of a language law, French still had the character of an official language.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156">\n        <a href="#cite_note-156">\n         [156]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the Constitution of 2007, Malagasy remained the national language while official languages were reintroduced: Malagasy, French, and English.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157">\n        <a href="#cite_note-157">\n         [157]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       English was removed as an official language from the constitution approved by voters in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_constitutional_referendum,_2010" title="Malagasy constitutional referendum, 2010">\n        November 2010 referendum\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4thRepublic_1-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-4thRepublic-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The outcome of the referendum, and its consequences for official and national language policy, are not recognized by the political opposition, who cite lack of transparency and inclusiveness in the way the election was organized by the\n       <a href="/wiki/High_Transitional_Authority" title="High Transitional Authority">\n        High Transitional Authority\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crisisgroup_104-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-crisisgroup-104">\n         [104]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Language Policy\n       </b>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Over the years, Madagascar has had different language policies under different influences of authority. The indigenous language of Madagascar, Malagasy, was the predominant language on the island until the French colonization in 1897. Malagasy has developed throughout the decades from an oral language to a language that has a written system (Latin orthography), a change that was enforced by King Radama I, in 1823. Following the French colonization, the language of instruction and media changed from Malagasy to almost exclusively French. Moreover, the first French governor-general, Gallieni, also encouraged the French officials to learn Malagasy as well. After the advent of the Malagasy independence, the Madagascans tried to reinstate Malagasy as a language of instruction especially in secondary schools. However, the language policy was inadequately planned and Malagasy was struggling to surpass French as the language of instruction.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">\n        <a href="#cite_note-158">\n         [158]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Today, Madagascar has two official languages: Malagasy and French. Madagascar managed to maintain the indigenous language, Malagasy, in society and in schools despite the colonizing power. Malagasy and French are both the language of instruction in primary and secondary schools in Madagascar. The inclusion of the African language as a medium of instruction is usually uncommon in other colonized African countries.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">\n        <a href="#cite_note-159">\n         [159]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">\n        Religion\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Religion">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Religion_in_Madagascar" title="Religion in Madagascar">\n        Religion in Madagascar\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft" style="">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:200px">\n        <div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black">\n         <div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 2651.325628724px; border-left-color:Grey">\n         </div>\n         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Grey">\n         </div>\n         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Grey">\n         </div>\n         <div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 196.26105055052px; border-left-color:Red">\n         </div>\n         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Red">\n         </div>\n         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Red">\n         </div>\n         <div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 106.48918403248px; border-left-color:Green">\n         </div>\n         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Green">\n         </div>\n         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Green">\n         </div>\n         <div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 72.654252800537px; border-left-color:Blue">\n         </div>\n         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Blue">\n         </div>\n         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Blue">\n         </div>\n         <div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 62.584050111869px; border-left-color:Yellow">\n         </div>\n         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Yellow">\n         </div>\n         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Yellow">\n         </div>\n         <div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:0; border-width:0 370.10276951873px 100px 0; border-right-color:Purple">\n         </div>\n         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;right:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 100px 0;border-color:Purple">\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <p>\n          Religion in Madagascar (2010) according to the\n          <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">\n           Pew Research Center\n          </a>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pew_160-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-pew-160">\n            [160]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </p>\n         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">\n          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Purple; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n          </span>\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">\n           Protestant\n          </a>\n          (45.8%)\n         </div>\n         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">\n          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Yellow; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n          </span>\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">\n           Roman Catholic\n          </a>\n          (38.1%)\n         </div>\n         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">\n          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Blue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n          </span>\n          Other Christian (1.1%)\n         </div>\n         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">\n          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Green; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n          </span>\n          <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">\n           Muslim\n          </a>\n          (3%)\n         </div>\n         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">\n          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Red; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n          </span>\n          <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">\n           Folk religions\n          </a>\n          (4.5%)\n         </div>\n         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">\n          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Grey; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">\n          </span>\n          Unaffiliated (6.9%)\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Famadihana_reburial_razana_ancestor_Madagascar.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4288" data-file-width="2848" height="256" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Famadihana_reburial_razana_ancestor_Madagascar.jpg/170px-Famadihana_reburial_razana_ancestor_Madagascar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Famadihana_reburial_razana_ancestor_Madagascar.jpg/255px-Famadihana_reburial_razana_ancestor_Madagascar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Famadihana_reburial_razana_ancestor_Madagascar.jpg/340px-Famadihana_reburial_razana_ancestor_Madagascar.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Famadihana_reburial_razana_ancestor_Madagascar.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A\n         <a href="/wiki/Famadihana" title="Famadihana">\n          Famadihana\n         </a>\n         reburial ceremony.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       According to the US Department of State, 41% of Madagascans practice Christianity and 52% practice traditional religion,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BGNote_14-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BGNote-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       which tends to emphasize links between the living and the\n       <i>\n        razana\n       </i>\n       (ancestors). The\n       <a href="/wiki/Veneration_of_the_dead" title="Veneration of the dead">\n        veneration of ancestors\n       </a>\n       has led to the widespread tradition of tomb building, as well as the highlands practice of the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Famadihana" title="Famadihana">\n         famadihana\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , whereby a deceased family member\'s remains are exhumed and re-wrapped in fresh silk shrouds, before being replaced in the tomb. The famadihana is an occasion to celebrate the beloved ancestor\'s memory, reunite with family and community, and enjoy a festive atmosphere. Residents of surrounding villages are often invited to attend the party, where food and rum are typically served and a\n       <a href="/wiki/Hiragasy" title="Hiragasy">\n        hiragasy\n       </a>\n       troupe or other musical entertainment is commonly present.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-famadihana_161-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-famadihana-161">\n         [161]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Consideration for ancestors is also demonstrated through adherence to\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Fady_(taboo)" title="Fady (taboo)">\n         fady\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , taboos that are respected during and after the lifetime of the person who establishes them. It is widely believed that by showing respect for ancestors in these ways, they may intervene on behalf of the living. Conversely, misfortunes are often attributed to ancestors whose memory or wishes have been neglected. The sacrifice of zebu is a traditional method used to appease or honor the ancestors. In addition, the Malagasy traditionally believe in a creator god, called Zanahary or Andriamanitra.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bradtbeliefs_162-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bradtbeliefs-162">\n         [162]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       According to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">\n        Pew Research Center\n       </a>\n       , only 4.5% of Madagascans practice folk religions and 85% are\n       <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Madagascar" title="Christianity in Madagascar">\n        Christian\n       </a>\n       , with practitioners of Protestantism outnumbering adherents to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Madagascar" title="Roman Catholicism in Madagascar">\n        Roman Catholicism\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pew_160-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pew-160">\n         [160]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 1818, the\n       <a href="/wiki/London_Missionary_Society" title="London Missionary Society">\n        London Missionary Society\n       </a>\n       sent the first Christian missionaries to the island, where they built churches, translated the Bible into the Malagasy language and began to gain converts. Beginning in 1835, Queen\n       <a href="/wiki/Ranavalona_I" title="Ranavalona I">\n        Ranavalona I\n       </a>\n       persecuted these converts as part of an attempt to halt European cultural and political influence on the island. In 1869, a successor, Queen\n       <a href="/wiki/Ranavalona_II" title="Ranavalona II">\n        Ranavalona II\n       </a>\n       , converted the court to Christianity and encouraged Christian missionary activity, burning the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Sampy" title="Sampy">\n         sampy\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (royal idols) in a symbolic break with traditional beliefs.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163">\n        <a href="#cite_note-163">\n         [163]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Today, many Christians integrate their religious beliefs with traditional ones related to honoring the ancestors. For instance, they may bless their dead at church before proceeding with traditional burial rites or invite a\n       <a href="/wiki/Minister_(Christianity)" title="Minister (Christianity)">\n        Christian minister\n       </a>\n       to consecrate a\n       <i>\n        famadihana\n       </i>\n       reburial.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-famadihana_161-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-famadihana-161">\n         [161]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Malagasy Council of Churches comprises the four oldest and most prominent Christian denominations of Madagascar (Roman Catholic,\n       <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Jesus_Christ_in_Madagascar" title="Church of Jesus Christ in Madagascar">\n        Church of Jesus Christ in Madagascar\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_Lutheran_Church" title="Malagasy Lutheran Church">\n        Lutheran\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglican" title="Anglican">\n        Anglican\n       </a>\n       ) and has been an influential force in Malagasy politics.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USSD_164-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USSD-164">\n         [164]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">\n        Islam\n       </a>\n       is also practiced on the island. Islam was first brought to Madagascar in the Middle Ages by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab_people" title="Arab people">\n        Arab\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Somali_people" title="Somali people">\n        Somali\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">\n        Muslim\n       </a>\n       traders, who established several Islamic schools along the eastern coast. While the use of Arabic script and loan words and the adoption of Islamic astrology would spread across the island, the Islamic religion failed to take hold in all but a handful of southeastern coastal communities. Today,\n       <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Madagascar" title="Islam in Madagascar">\n        Muslims\n       </a>\n       constitute 7\xe2\x80\x933\xc2\xa0percent of the population of Madagascar and are largely concentrated in the northwestern provinces of\n       <a href="/wiki/Mahajanga" title="Mahajanga">\n        Mahajanga\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Antsiranana" title="Antsiranana">\n        Antsiranana\n       </a>\n       . The vast majority of\n       <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">\n        Muslims\n       </a>\n       are\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunni" title="Sunni">\n        Sunni\n       </a>\n       . Muslims are divided between those of Malagasy ethnicity,\n       <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_India" title="Demographics of India">\n        Indians\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Demography_of_Pakistan" title="Demography of Pakistan">\n        Pakistanis\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Comoros" title="Comoros">\n        Comorians\n       </a>\n       . More recently,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">\n        Hinduism\n       </a>\n       was introduced to Madagascar through\n       <a href="/wiki/Gujarati_people" title="Gujarati people">\n        Gujarati people\n       </a>\n       immigrating from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Saurashtra_(region)" title="Saurashtra (region)">\n        Saurashtra\n       </a>\n       region of\n       <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">\n        India\n       </a>\n       in the late 19th century. Most Hindus in Madagascar speak\n       <a href="/wiki/Gujarati_language" title="Gujarati language">\n        Gujarati\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">\n        Hindi\n       </a>\n       at home.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-id_165-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-id-165">\n         [165]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">\n        Culture\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Culture">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Madagascar" title="Culture of Madagascar">\n        Culture of Madagascar\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Each of the many ethnic sub-groups in Madagascar adhere to their own set of beliefs, practices and ways of life that have historically contributed to their unique identities. However, there are a number of core cultural features that are common throughout the island, creating a strongly unified Malagasy cultural identity. In addition to a common language and shared traditional religious beliefs around a creator god and veneration of the ancestors, the traditional Malagasy worldview is shaped by values that emphasize\n       <i>\n        fihavanana\n       </i>\n       (solidarity),\n       <i>\n        vintana\n       </i>\n       (destiny),\n       <i>\n        tody\n       </i>\n       (karma), and\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Hasina_(Madagascar)" title="Hasina (Madagascar)">\n         hasina\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , a sacred life force that traditional communities believe imbues and thereby legitimates authority figures within the community or family. Other cultural elements commonly found throughout the island include the practice of male circumcision; strong kinship ties; a widespread belief in the power of magic, diviners, astrology and witch doctors; and a traditional division of social classes into nobles, commoners, and slaves.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LOC_20-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-LOC-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bradtbeliefs_162-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bradtbeliefs-162">\n         [162]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Although social castes are no longer legally recognized, ancestral caste affiliation often continues to affect social status, economic opportunity and roles within the community.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166">\n        <a href="#cite_note-166">\n         [166]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Malagasy people traditionally consult\n       <i>\n        Mpanandro\n       </i>\n       ("Makers of the Days") to identify the most auspicious days for important events such as weddings or\n       <i>\n        famadihana\n       </i>\n       , according to a traditional astrological system introduced by Arabs. Similarly, the nobles of many Malagasy communities in the pre-colonial period would commonly employ advisers known as the\n       <i>\n        ombiasy\n       </i>\n       (from\n       <i>\n        olona-be-hasina\n       </i>\n       , "man of much virtue") of the southeastern\n       <a href="/wiki/Antemoro_people" title="Antemoro people">\n        Antemoro\n       </a>\n       ethnic group, who trace their ancestry back to early Arab settlers.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167">\n        <a href="#cite_note-167">\n         [167]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The diverse origins of Malagasy culture are evident in its tangible expressions. The most emblematic instrument of Madagascar, the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Valiha" title="Valiha">\n         valiha\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , is a\n       <a href="/wiki/Bamboo" title="Bamboo">\n        bamboo\n       </a>\n       tube\n       <a href="/wiki/Zither" title="Zither">\n        zither\n       </a>\n       carried to Madagascar by early settlers from\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Kalimantan" title="South Kalimantan">\n        southern Borneo\n       </a>\n       , and is very similar in form to those found in\n       <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Indonesia" title="Music of Indonesia">\n        Indonesia\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Music_of_the_Philippines" title="Music of the Philippines">\n        Philippines\n       </a>\n       today.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Blench.2C_R._1982_pp._81-93_168-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Blench.2C_R._1982_pp._81-93-168">\n         [168]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Traditional\n       <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Madagascar" title="Architecture of Madagascar">\n        houses in Madagascar\n       </a>\n       are likewise similar to those of southern Borneo in terms of symbolism and construction, featuring a rectangular layout with a peaked roof and central support pillar.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169">\n        <a href="#cite_note-169">\n         [169]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Reflecting a widespread veneration of the ancestors, tombs are culturally significant in many regions and tend to be built of more durable material, typically stone, and display more elaborate decoration than the houses of the living.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Acquier.2C_Jean-Louis._170-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Acquier.2C_Jean-Louis.-170">\n         [170]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The production and weaving of silk can be traced back to the island\'s earliest settlers, and Madagascar\'s national dress, the woven\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Lamba_(garment)" title="Lamba (garment)">\n         lamba\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , has evolved into a varied and refined art.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171">\n        <a href="#cite_note-171">\n         [171]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Southeast Asian cultural influence is also evident in\n       <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_cuisine" title="Malagasy cuisine">\n        Malagasy cuisine\n       </a>\n       , in which rice is consumed at every meal, typically accompanied by one of a variety of flavorful vegetable or meat dishes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Antal_172-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Antal-172">\n         [172]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       African influence is reflected in the sacred importance of zebu cattle and their embodiment of their owner\'s wealth, traditions originating on the African mainland.\n       <a href="/wiki/Cattle_raiding" title="Cattle raiding">\n        Cattle rustling\n       </a>\n       , originally a rite of passage for young men in the plains areas of Madagascar where the largest herds of cattle are kept, has become a dangerous and sometimes deadly criminal enterprise as herdsmen in the southwest attempt to defend their cattle with traditional spears against increasingly armed professional rustlers.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Camp93_70-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Camp93-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">\n        Arts\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Arts">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hira_gasy_dancer_Madagascar.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3712" data-file-width="2272" height="278" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Hira_gasy_dancer_Madagascar.jpg/170px-Hira_gasy_dancer_Madagascar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Hira_gasy_dancer_Madagascar.jpg/255px-Hira_gasy_dancer_Madagascar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Hira_gasy_dancer_Madagascar.jpg/340px-Hira_gasy_dancer_Madagascar.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hira_gasy_dancer_Madagascar.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A\n         <a href="/wiki/Hiragasy" title="Hiragasy">\n          Hiragasy\n         </a>\n         dancer.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A wide variety of oral and written\n       <a href="/wiki/Literature_of_Madagascar" title="Literature of Madagascar">\n        literature\n       </a>\n       has developed in Madagascar. One of the island\'s foremost artistic traditions is its\n       <a href="/wiki/Hainteny" title="Hainteny">\n        oratory\n       </a>\n       , as expressed in the forms of\n       <i>\n        hainteny\n       </i>\n       (poetry),\n       <i>\n        kabary\n       </i>\n       (public discourse) and\n       <i>\n        ohabolana\n       </i>\n       (proverbs).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173">\n        <a href="#cite_note-173">\n         [173]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Madatana_174-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Madatana-174">\n         [174]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       An epic poem exemplifying these traditions, the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Ibonia" title="Ibonia">\n         Ibonia\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , has been handed down over the centuries in several different forms across the island, and offers insight into the diverse mythologies and beliefs of traditional Malagasy communities.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175">\n        <a href="#cite_note-175">\n         [175]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This tradition was continued in the 20th century by such artists as\n       <a href="/wiki/Jean-Joseph_Rabearivelo" title="Jean-Joseph Rabearivelo">\n        Jean-Joseph Rabearivelo\n       </a>\n       , who is considered Africa\'s first modern poet,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176">\n        <a href="#cite_note-176">\n         [176]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Elie_Rajaonarison" title="Elie Rajaonarison">\n        Elie Rajaonarison\n       </a>\n       , an exemplar of the new wave of Malagasy poetry.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177">\n        <a href="#cite_note-177">\n         [177]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Madagascar has also developed a rich\n       <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Madagascar" title="Music of Madagascar">\n        musical heritage\n       </a>\n       , embodied in dozens of regional musical genres such as the coastal\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Salegy" title="Salegy">\n         salegy\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       or highland\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Hiragasy" title="Hiragasy">\n         hiragasy\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       that enliven village gatherings, local dance floors and national airwaves.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Randrianary_178-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Randrianary-178">\n         [178]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Additionally, Madagascar also has a growing culture of classical music fostered through youth academies, organizations and orchestras that promote youth involvement in classical music.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The plastic arts are also widespread throughout the island. In addition to the tradition of silk weaving and lamba production, the weaving of\n       <a href="/wiki/Raffia_palm" title="Raffia palm">\n        raffia\n       </a>\n       and other local plant materials has been used to create a wide array of practical items such as floor mats, baskets, purses and hats.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-handicrafts_140-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-handicrafts-140">\n         [140]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Wood carving is a highly developed art form, with distinct regional styles evident in the decoration of balcony railings and other architectural elements. Sculptors create a variety of furniture and household goods,\n       <i>\n        aloalo\n       </i>\n       funerary posts, and wooden sculptures, many of which are produced for the tourist market.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Terrible_179-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Terrible-179">\n         [179]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The decorative and functional woodworking traditions of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Zafimaniry" title="Zafimaniry">\n        Zafimaniry\n       </a>\n       people of the central highlands was inscribed on UNESCO\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_Intangible_Cultural_Heritage_Lists" title="UNESCO Intangible Cultural Heritage Lists">\n        list of Intangible Cultural Heritage\n       </a>\n       in 2008.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180">\n        <a href="#cite_note-180">\n         [180]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Among the Antaimoro people, the production of paper embedded with flowers and other decorative natural materials is a long-established tradition that the community has begun to market to eco-tourists.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Terrible_179-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Terrible-179">\n         [179]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Embroidery" title="Embroidery">\n        Embroidery\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Drawn_thread_work" title="Drawn thread work">\n        drawn thread work\n       </a>\n       are done by hand to produce clothing, as well as tablecloths and other home textiles for sale in local crafts markets.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-handicrafts_140-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-handicrafts-140">\n         [140]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A small but growing number of fine art galleries in Antananarivo, and several other urban areas, offer paintings by local artists, and annual art events, such as the Hosotra open-air exhibition in the capital, contribute to the continuing development of fine arts in Madagascar.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181">\n        <a href="#cite_note-181">\n         [181]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sport_and_recreation">\n        Sport and recreation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Sport and recreation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moraingy_fighting_Madagascar_sport.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1301" data-file-width="1617" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Moraingy_fighting_Madagascar_sport.jpg/230px-Moraingy_fighting_Madagascar_sport.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Moraingy_fighting_Madagascar_sport.jpg/345px-Moraingy_fighting_Madagascar_sport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Moraingy_fighting_Madagascar_sport.jpg/460px-Moraingy_fighting_Madagascar_sport.jpg 2x" width="230"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moraingy_fighting_Madagascar_sport.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Moraingy" title="Moraingy">\n           Moraingy\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         is a traditional martial art of Madagascar.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A number of traditional pastimes have emerged in Madagascar.\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Moraingy" title="Moraingy">\n         Moraingy\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , a type of hand-to-hand combat, is a popular spectator sport in coastal regions. It is traditionally practiced by men, but women have recently begun to participate.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182">\n        <a href="#cite_note-182">\n         [182]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The wrestling of\n       <a href="/wiki/Zebu" title="Zebu">\n        zebu\n       </a>\n       cattle, which is named\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Savika&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Savika (page does not exist)">\n        savika\n       </a>\n       or\n       <i>\n        tolon-omby\n       </i>\n       , is also practiced in many regions.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lambatradition_183-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-lambatradition-183">\n         [183]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In addition to sports, a wide variety of games are played. Among the most emblematic is\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Fanorona" title="Fanorona">\n         fanorona\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , a board game widespread throughout the Highland regions. According to folk legend, the succession of King\n       <a href="/wiki/Andrianjaka" title="Andrianjaka">\n        Andrianjaka\n       </a>\n       after his father\n       <a href="/wiki/Ralambo" title="Ralambo">\n        Ralambo\n       </a>\n       was partially due to the obsession that Andrianjaka\'s older brother may have had with playing\n       <i>\n        fanorona\n       </i>\n       to the detriment of his other responsibilities.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iarivo_184-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-iarivo-184">\n         [184]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Western recreational activities were introduced to Madagascar over the past two centuries.\n       <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_in_Madagascar" title="Rugby union in Madagascar">\n        Rugby union\n       </a>\n       is considered the national sport of Madagascar.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185">\n        <a href="#cite_note-185">\n         [185]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Madagascar" title="Football in Madagascar">\n        Soccer\n       </a>\n       is also popular. Madagascar has produced a world champion in\n       <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A9tanque" title="P\xc3\xa9tanque">\n        p\xc3\xa9tanque\n       </a>\n       , a French game similar to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lawn_bowling" title="Lawn bowling">\n        lawn bowling\n       </a>\n       , which is widely played in urban areas and throughout the Highlands.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186">\n        <a href="#cite_note-186">\n         [186]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       School athletics programs typically include soccer, track and field, judo, boxing, women\'s basketball and women\'s tennis. Madagascar sent its first competitors to the Olympic Games in 1964 and has also competed in the African Games.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EBLand_19-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EBLand-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Scouting" title="Scouting">\n        Scouting\n       </a>\n       is represented in Madagascar by its\n       <a href="/wiki/Firaisan%27ny_Skotisma_eto_Madagasikara" title="Firaisan\'ny Skotisma eto Madagasikara">\n        own local federation\n       </a>\n       of three scouting clubs. Membership in 2011 was estimated at 14,905.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Census_2010_187-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Census_2010-187">\n         [187]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Because of its advanced sports facilities,\n       <a href="/wiki/Antananarivo" title="Antananarivo">\n        Antananarivo\n       </a>\n       gained the hosting rights for several of Africa\'s top international basketball events, including the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2011_FIBA_Africa_Championship" title="2011 FIBA Africa Championship">\n        2011 FIBA Africa Championship\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188">\n        <a href="#cite_note-188">\n         [188]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the\n       <a href="/wiki/2009_FIBA_Africa_Championship_for_Women" title="2009 FIBA Africa Championship for Women">\n        2009 FIBA Africa Championship for Women\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189">\n        <a href="#cite_note-189">\n         [189]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the\n       <a href="/wiki/2014_FIBA_Africa_Under-18_Championship" title="2014 FIBA Africa Under-18 Championship">\n        2014 FIBA Africa Under-18 Championship\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190">\n        <a href="#cite_note-190">\n         [190]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the\n       <a href="/wiki/2013_FIBA_Africa_Under-16_Championship" title="2013 FIBA Africa Under-16 Championship">\n        2013 FIBA Africa Under-16 Championship\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191">\n        <a href="#cite_note-191">\n         [191]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/2015_FIBA_Africa_Under-16_Championship_for_Women" title="2015 FIBA Africa Under-16 Championship for Women">\n        2015 FIBA Africa Under-16 Championship for Women\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192">\n        <a href="#cite_note-192">\n         [192]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">\n        Cuisine\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Cuisine">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_cuisine" title="Malagasy cuisine">\n        Malagasy cuisine\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Malagasy cuisine reflects the diverse influences of Southeast Asian, African, Indian, Chinese and European culinary traditions. The complexity of Malagasy meals can range from the simple, traditional preparations introduced by the earliest settlers, to the refined festival dishes prepared for the island\'s 19th-century monarchs. Throughout almost the entire island, the contemporary cuisine of Madagascar typically consists of a base of rice (\n       <i>\n        vary\n       </i>\n       ) served with an accompaniment (\n       <i>\n        laoka\n       </i>\n       ). The many varieties of laoka may be\n       <a href="/wiki/Vegetarian_cuisine" title="Vegetarian cuisine">\n        vegetarian\n       </a>\n       or include animal proteins, and typically feature a sauce flavored with such ingredients as ginger, onion, garlic, tomato, vanilla, coconut milk,\n       <a href="/wiki/Sodium_chloride" title="Sodium chloride">\n        salt\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Curry_powder" title="Curry powder">\n        curry powder\n       </a>\n       , green peppercorns or, less commonly, other spices or herbs. In parts of the arid south and west,\n       <a href="/wiki/Pastoralism" title="Pastoralism">\n        pastoral\n       </a>\n       families may replace rice with maize,\n       <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">\n        cassava\n       </a>\n       , or\n       <a href="/wiki/Curd" title="Curd">\n        curds\n       </a>\n       made from fermented zebu milk. A wide variety of sweet and savory\n       <a href="/wiki/Fritter" title="Fritter">\n        fritters\n       </a>\n       as well as other street foods are available across the island, as are diverse tropical and temperate-climate fruits. Locally produced beverages include fruit juices, coffee,\n       <a href="/wiki/Herbal_tea" title="Herbal tea">\n        herbal teas\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Tea" title="Tea">\n        teas\n       </a>\n       , and alcoholic drinks such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Rum" title="Rum">\n        rum\n       </a>\n       , wine, and beer.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Antal_172-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Antal-172">\n         [172]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Three_Horses_Beer" title="Three Horses Beer">\n        Three Horses Beer\n       </a>\n       is the most popular beer on the island\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THBpilsner_193-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-THBpilsner-193">\n         [193]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and is considered emblematic of Madagascar.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-promos_194-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-promos-194">\n         [194]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The island also produces some of the world\'s finest chocolate;\n       <a href="/wiki/Chocolaterie_Robert" title="Chocolaterie Robert">\n        Chocolaterie Robert\n       </a>\n       , established in 1940, is the most famous chocolate company on the island.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-prize_195-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-prize-195">\n         [195]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: See also">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n       <ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">\n        <li style="display:table-row">\n         <span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center">\n          <img alt="flag" class="noviewer thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="21" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Flag_of_Madagascar.svg/32px-Flag_of_Madagascar.svg.png"     <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Outline_of_Madagascar" title="Outline of Madagascar">\n         Outline of Madagascar\n        </a>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">\n        Notes\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Madagascar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Notes">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 25em; -webkit-column-width: 25em; column-width: 25em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n       <ol class="references">\n        <li id="cite_note-4thRepublic-1">\n         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n          ^\n          <a href="#cite_ref-4thRepublic_1-0">\n           <sup>\n            <i>\n             <b>\n              a\n             </b>\n            </i>\n           </sup>\n          </a>\n          <a href="#cite_ref-4thRepublic_1-1">\n           <sup>\n            <i>\n             <b>\n              b\n             </b>\n            </i>\n           </sup>\n          </a>\n         </span>\n         <span class="reference-text">\n          <cite class="citation web">\n           Le Comit\xc3\xa9 Consultatif Constitutionnel (1 October 2010).\n           <a class="external text" href="https://www.webcitation.org/61BvMnZmH" rel="nofollow">\n            "\n            <i>\n             Projet de Constitution de la Quatri\xc3\xa8me R\xc3\xa9publique de Madagascar\n            </i>\n            "\n           </a>\n           (in French).
